Important News 2

The Explosion at the Jinan Ammunition Depot 53

The Number of Casualties is Still Under Investigation

Approximately Several Hundred Houses Destroyed

The ammunition depot inside Jinan Communications City, by Daming Lake, suddenly exploded one evening with a thunderous sound. Those who were unaware of the true situation were shocked and doubtful. Here is a detailed account of the circumstances:

Location and History of the Depot: There are two ammunition depots within Jinan City, by Daming Lake. One is west of Beiji Pavilion, facing east, and the other, the site of the incident, is east of Beimen (the North Gate, which is a water gate, is closed year-round and has a building above it called "Bo"). This one is called the East Depot. It has few buildings and mainly stores discarded ammunition. A platoon of soldiers from the 11th Company, 3rd Battalion, 2nd Regiment of the Shandong Garrison Brigade is stationed there for guard duty. Outside, there are two depot guards. To the east of this depot is Xiaobeimen, which has long been blocked up. There is also a Shuiyue Nunnery, where the Third Outpost of the Second Public Security Bureau in the city is stationed, with fourteen police officers. These two ammunition depots originally belonged to the Jinan Arsenal in the new city. Last month, the arsenal of the General Headquarters (Hong Zi Ao) stored a large amount of lead from ammunition sold during the late Qing Dynasty. Since it was neither destroyed nor had a place to be stored, it was discussed with the arsenal to temporarily store it there. It is said that a total of one million pounds of old black powder, three to four hundred thousand rounds of bullets and lead pellets, more than twenty landmines, and an unknown number of mortar shells were stored.

City-wide Curfew During the Explosion: At 8:45 PM on the first day, the sky was gloomy. Suddenly, sparks burst out from the northern part of the city, followed by a deafening roar. The roof tiles of the entire city shook, and thick smoke billowed straight up. A strong wind rose suddenly, and soon after, a series of cannon-like sounds rumbled, numbering more than a dozen. The people on the streets suspected a great disaster was imminent and fled in panic. All the shops closed, and the cries of women and children were mixed in, creating great disorder. Several minutes later, the Garrison Headquarters learned that it was the ammunition depot that had exploded. However, they did not know if there were any survivors inside, so they ordered a special curfew. All the garrison brigade troops, Public Security Bureau police, and others were dispatched to cut off traffic. The military police in the east city were so close to the ammunition depot that they did not know the real situation after the explosion. Some even lay on the ground holding their guns, ready to fire. The seriousness of the situation was unprecedented. At 9:30 PM, the third passenger train on the Jiaoji Railway arrived in Jinan. Passengers disembarked, but since they could not walk on the streets, they all slept in the station. At this time, Garrison Commander Shi Zhongcheng led his troops to the scene to investigate and maintain order. Public Security Bureau Chief Li Yue also led the fire brigade and security team to put out the remaining fire. Chief of Staff Li Zhongkang of the General Headquarters and Jinan Mayor Zhao Jingshi also arrived to inspect the scene. Afterwards, people were sent to guard it. Although the cause of the incident is unknown, it is the responsibility of the ammunition depot officer, Wang Keming, who failed to inspect properly. He will be placed in custody.

Public Notice to Reassure the People After the Incident: From the explosion at 8:45 PM until about 10:00 PM, the cause became clear, and the situation on the streets eased slightly. The Garrison Headquarters and the Public Security Bureau both issued public notices to reassure the people. However, it was already the time of the regular curfew, and there was no one on the streets. The Garrison Headquarters' notice stated: "At 8:00 PM today, a sudden explosion occurred. It was the ammunition stored in the ammunition depot east of Beiji Pavilion that exploded due to hot weather. There are no other circumstances. This notice is issued to inform all merchants and residents to be aware and not to panic. This notice." The Jinan Public Security Bureau's notice stated: "At 8:30 PM this evening, the Eastern Ammunition Depot of the ordnance depot at Xiaobeimen accidentally exploded, causing ammunition to detonate. The fire has now been extinguished, and there is no danger. This notice is issued to inform all to be aware and not to panic or cause disturbances. Strictly this notice."

Losses and Aftermath: This morning (the 2nd), the military cleared the site of the incident and investigated the losses. It was determined that only gunpowder, bullets, and the like had exploded. Fortunately, the twenty landmines did not ignite, otherwise, the situation would have been even more unimaginable. The ammunition depot buildings were all destroyed. The buildings of the Shuiyue Nunnery to the east were also toppled. Two ammunition depot guards were killed, and seven were seriously injured. It was said that the depot soldiers who were sleeping indoors that night were all killed by the explosion. Some bodies were thrown so far by the force of the explosion that they could not be found. Those who were outdoors were mostly unharmed. Out of the twelve police officers at the Shuiyue Nunnery, except for four who were on duty, the remaining eight who were indoors were all injured. The Baiyi Nunnery south of the ammunition depot also had people seriously injured. In addition, in nearby Lishan Street, a 21-year-old woman surnamed Wang who had just given birth was holding her baby. That evening, both her legs were blown off by the shells, and the baby's head was half blown off. Mother and child both died without medical attention. In the vicinity of the ammunition depot, such as Beiji Pavilion Street and Lishan Street, seven or eight out of ten houses collapsed. Only a few remained. Many houses were also destroyed in areas such as Zhang Gong祠, San Gong祠, Huibo Temple Street, He Sheng Battleground, and Qiuyayuan, numbering no less than several hundred. Many people were crushed and injured. The number is still under detailed investigation. It was said that when the explosion occurred, lake water overflowed onto the shore. However, Huibo Tower, which is only five zhang away from the ammunition depot, was unharmed, which is also a miracle. Today, the provincial government held a memorial week for the Premier. Acting Chairman Zhu Xi reported on the incident and said that those who were killed and injured would be compensated. The Provincial Consolidation Committee will handle this matter. The detailed arrangements have not yet been determined.

Conflicting Accounts of the Cause of the Explosion: At the time of the incident, some suspected it was the work of the enemy, but this has now been proven incorrect. As for the cause, there are various rumors. Those who were at the scene were either dead or seriously injured, making it impossible to inquire. Some say that the gunpowder had been stored for many years and should have been destroyed. It seemed unsuitable for destroying enemies, yet it was not useless. If it was stored improperly, it was more than enough to explode. The gunpowder was stored in iron boxes, but the boxes were damaged. Then, wooden boxes were added, but the wooden boxes were also damaged. Now, it is mostly packed in sacks. Although it does not matter if the sacks are old, it is most important to avoid sacks that have contained salt because gunpowder explodes when it comes into contact with salt. It is possible that some of these sacks contained salt. This is one theory. Some say that the guards and depot soldiers, numbering over a dozen, were too many, and some must have had a habit of smoking cigarettes, causing a fire. This is the second theory. Others say that when storing gunpowder, cold water must be poured on it when the weather gets too hot to a certain degree. Recently, the weather in Jinan has been hot and dry. The depot soldiers may have forgotten to pour water because that day was the old Dragon Boat Festival, and they were drinking and celebrating. This led to the explosion. This is the third theory. Based on the circumstances, the latter theory seems more likely. (June 2nd)

Shen Honglie Arrives in Qingdao to Inspect Defense 54

Qingdao Communication: Shen Honglie, Commander of the Northeast Navy in Qingdao, arrived in Laoshan Bay from Changshan Island on the 26th of last month. He has been inspecting the defense situation there for several days. Now that he has finished, he returned to Qingdao on the Haihe warship on the 30th and convened a naval defense conference at the headquarters that evening, gathering important personnel from the department and captains of the various ships stationed in Qingdao to discuss coastal defense. On the 1st of this month, Shen took advantage of a Sunday and specially invited the consuls of the four countries of Britain, America, France, and Germany to travel to Laoshan on the Zhenhai warship to visit various scenic spots. He returned to Qingdao on the same warship that evening. I (Fool) went to the Naval Headquarters to meet him today (2nd), but Shen was out. The head of the Naval Qingdao Office, Li Yucheng, received me. Li said the following: "Commander Shen's return to Qingdao this time is purely for inspection purposes. The rumor that Shen will be the mayor of Qingdao is completely unfounded and has no basis. There are currently four ships of the First Fleet stationed in Qingdao, namely, the Haiqi, Haichen, Zhaohe, and Jinghai. The defense of Qingdao is safe and worry-free. A few days ago, the Jiangli warship carried about 150 marines to Dongjiakou and Gongkou to suppress bandits. We have now received a report that the bandits there have been completely eliminated and will be able to return to Qingdao in about 10 days. Also, the Qingyang Station on the Jiaoji Railway originally had a company of marines stationed there. Now, we feel that the force is weak, so we plan to send another company there tomorrow to increase the defense. In this way, the water and land defense will be more consolidated, and the citizens of Qingdao can rest easy. Zhang Xueliang, Commander of the Northeast, has always taken protecting the territory and ensuring the safety of the people as his duty. The navy's actions will follow Zhang's lead." (June 2nd)

Guangzhou Cracks Down on Important Communist Party Organs 56

Guangzhou Communication: Recently, the Communist Party in Guangdong Province has once again plotted to carry out activities. In addition to the Communist bandits ravaging various places in the Dongjiang region, Communist Party propaganda and printed materials have also been repeatedly discovered in Guangzhou. A few days ago, at a rally held in the playground of Zhongshan University to welcome triumphant soldiers from all walks of life, three young people were arrested by detectives for distributing Communist Party leaflets. On the evening of the 25th, at about 8:00 PM, a long-distance bus from Xihaokou to Yonghan Road in the city was suddenly boarded by more than a dozen people resembling workers. Two of them pulled out guns and pointed them at the driver, while the others scattered a large bundle of reactionary leaflets along the way until they reached a crowded area on Yonghan Road, where they fled one after another. The following evening, near the Wuxianmen of Changdi, several members of the Communist Party stacked no less than several thousand leaflets printed in red ink in a dark corner in front of a store after nightfall. Fearing that people would not notice, they set off a large bundle of firecrackers in the area. After the sound of the firecrackers, passers-by stopped to watch, and only then did they realize that a large number of Communist Party propaganda items had been found there. By the time the detectives arrived, the party members had already fled far away, and they had to collect the printed materials, report the case, and burn them. After repeated discoveries of this kind of incident in the city, the Public Security Bureau paid special attention and, fearing that the Communist Party would take the opportunity to cause trouble during the upcoming anniversary of the May 30th Massacre, ordered the subordinate detective teams to intensify their investigations and interrogate the Communist Party members arrested a few days ago. After learning some clues, on the 27th, based on the report of a secret agent, they discovered various secret organizations formed by senior members sent by Moscow to Guangdong Province. After receiving the report, the Public Security Bureau made arrangements overnight to encircle and arrest them in separate ways. Because they were informed that the party was planning to riot on May 30th, they had to quickly take measures to suppress and prevent chaos from arising. That night, several armored vehicles were prepared in front of the Public Security Bureau, and three large security teams divided into three groups to search the addresses. First, they went to Xinfeng Street, behind the corner of the Provincial Government Office, and surrounded the Datong Medical Clinic on that street. The medical clinic was the highest organ of the Guangdong Communist Party organized by the Communist Party. When the troops entered the clinic to search and arrest, the main leaders of the Communist Party were holding a meeting in the secret room of the clinic. More than a dozen members of the party were captured in one fell swoop. The Communist Party also confessed without denial because the matter had been exposed. The most important person was Zhuang, and there were also several female Communist Party members, among whom Chen admitted to being the secretary, and all the leaflets had been drafted by her. The other three were a head of documents and two secretaries. In addition, they seized a total of four large rattan boxes of Communist Party documents and leaflets. That same evening, they also cracked down on the secretarial office and printing press of the Communist Party in a residence in Laojia Alley, Huifudong Road, and seized several male and female Communist Party members. It was found that the Communist Party members arrested this time were rarely young people but were mostly elderly and corrupt. Most of the female party members had bound feet and dressed like servants. At first glance, they were not figures of the new era. From this, it was learned that the party had changed its plan for using personnel in order to conceal them from the outside world. During the interrogation, both male and female Communist Party members wrote their confessions in their own handwriting. Among them, the main leaders could speak Russian, indicating that they were all sent south by the Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union to carry out activities. (May 31st)

Appendix: The Hong Kong newspaper reported the following: A few days ago, reactionary leaflets were found in Guangzhou in Huangsha, Ruyifang, Xidi, the rooftop of the Daxin Company, and in front of the power company. After the arrest of the Communist Party members at the Triumphant Rally, Liang Ziguang, the chief of the Public Security Bureau, believed that since the Communist Party was so rampant, there must be secret Communist Party locations in the city. He specially consulted with Director Ouyang and interrogated the Communist Party members arrested a few days ago at the Xianhu Street Gongxing Hotel and the Old Warehouse Alley Penglai Hotel overnight. After obtaining information about the various Communist Party organs, he and Deputy Captain Yuan Yaoxin led all the team members and armed police of the Security Brigade on the 27th and set off separately to encircle and arrest them at the locations provided. They did not stop until dawn that night, having cracked down on three Communist Party organs: one in the liberal arts dormitory of a certain university, one in the Datong Hospital on Xinfeng Street, and one in the Dajuesi Temple front Luzhou lane, under Yonghan Sub-Bureau. In total, tens of thousands of various reactionary leaflets and several printing presses were seized, along with four female Communist Party members and eight male Communist Party members. All the male Communist Party members were important figures in the Communist Party. The female party members all spoke with a Hainanese accent. Two of them were already over forty years old and had unbound feet. At first glance, they looked like country women. No one expected them to be Communist Party members. One of the youngest, about eighteen or nineteen years old, dressed like a maid and was the secretary of the Communist Party. When the detectives arrived, she was drafting her report to the Provincial Committee. All the Communist Party members confessed without denial after being arrested. The young female Communist Party member even admitted to distributing leaflets on the rooftop of the Daxin Company and that they were also responsible for distributing leaflets in front of the power company a few days ago. However, when they confessed to this point, all the Communist Party members regretted that this move was too radical and had attracted the attention of the authorities, leading to the destruction of the organs.

Hunan Commemorates the June 1st Massacre 57

Changsha Communication: Seven years have passed since the June 1st Massacre of Changsha citizens by the Japanese warship Fushimi Maru in the twelfth year of the Republic of China. Although the government has repeatedly urged a resolution, the Japanese side has repeatedly delayed it, and the case remains unresolved. The Hunan Provincial Education Association and the Abolish Treaty Association consider this case to be a unique and utter humiliation for the people of Hunan, who are directly oppressed by Japanese imperialists. They have jointly initiated a seventh-anniversary commemoration meeting at 9:30 AM today (June 1st) at the Zhongshan Hall of the Provincial Education Association. More than a thousand representatives from various agencies, organizations, and schools attended. After performing the rituals, Chairman Huang Xingyi reported on the significance of the meeting, stating that seven years have passed since the June 1st Massacre. The reason for the massacre was that Japanese imperialists used force to impose the Twenty-One Demands during Yuan Shikai's time, and the people of Hunan implemented an economic boycott against Japan. On the twelfth day, people from all walks of life were giving speeches along the river when the Japanese warship Fushimi Maru, which was docked in Changsha, ordered sailors to land and open fire on the people, killing and injuring more than a dozen people. Our commemoration today should urge the government to resolve this case as soon as possible to comfort the spirits of the dead and avenge the national humiliation. Next, Yang Xuancheng, the former negotiator representing the provincial government, reported that when this case occurred, he was responsible for the negotiations and felt very sad when he thought back. Because this case has been pending for a long time, he not only felt sorry for the deceased but also for the country. When the June 1st Movement occurred, the Japanese wanted him to ban the patriotic actions of the people. He replied that their actions were not out of line and it was inconvenient to ban them. Soon after, the Commercial Port Office reported that Japanese sailors had landed and killed people, so he immediately negotiated with the Japanese and proposed five demands: (1) Punish the murderers; (2) Apologize; (3) Replace the Japanese consul; (4) Withdraw the Japanese warship; (5) Compensate the dead and injured. At that time, the Japanese consul said that since you want to replace me, I am a responsible person and it is inconvenient to negotiate, so there was no result. In the thirteenth year, he went to Beijing to ask the former Ministry of Foreign Affairs to resolve the matter as soon as possible. The Japanese government said that all cases must be resolved together. Our negotiators had already been appointed, but the Japanese side delayed sending theirs, so it was suspended again. In the fourteenth year, the Japanese consul was replaced, and he negotiated with the new consul, Shimizu Hachiichi. In the winter of the fourteenth year, a resolution to mediate was reached, but the Japanese side wanted to avoid the apology. He said at the time that if the compensation was insufficient, our government could make up for it, but the apology was essential. After he left office in the fifteenth year, the situation was not very clear. His successor, Mr. Gong Debei, negotiated in various ways but could not get a result. Today, we hope that all comrades know why foreigners can kill our Chinese people with impunity and why foreign warships can come to China. This is because the former diplomats did not understand their responsibilities and feared foreigners. Therefore, he hoped that the Chinese people would not give up their rights again. Next, Zhang Jiong of the Provincial Party Committee spoke, hoping that everyone would work together to abolish unequal treaties and implement an economic boycott, fundamentally stopping the use of foreign goods. After the speeches, the chairman put forward the draft telegram for voting. The entire body passed it and then shouted slogans and dispersed. Appendix: The telegram is as follows: "The June 1st Massacre in Hunan is the most poisonous and evil fact of Japanese imperialists violating international law and harming our Chinese nation, and it is also one of the most shameful and tragic commemorations in Hunan. Seven years have passed since the occurrence of this case, but there has been no appropriate resolution. Today is the seventh anniversary of the June 1st Massacre. The representatives of our association, representing the people of Hunan, held a commemorative meeting at the Provincial Education Association at 9:00 AM this morning. More than seven speakers successively spoke about the tragedy and its suspension. The crowds were indignant and unanimously proposed to send a telegram to the central Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the provincial government to seriously negotiate with the Japanese side based on the five demands of the people of Hunan and resolve the June 1st Massacre as soon as possible. We also hope that the people of Hunan and compatriots from all provinces will unite and rise up to support the resolution of the June 1st Massacre in order to avenge the shame of the people of Hunan and comfort the souls of the martyrs who died on June 1st. The Provisional Telegram cannot express the extent of our indignation." (June 1st)

Panic Over the Rising Flood in Jin 58

Implementing Checks on Foreign Exchange

Taiyuan Communication: Recently, due to speculation and disruption of finance, prices have soared and foreign exchange rates have risen in the city of Jin, with remittances to Pingjin reaching more than 330 yuan. The entire city is in a state of panic. The authorities decided at a meeting a few days ago that the Finance Department, the Industry and Commerce Department, the Jin-Cha-Sui Gendarmerie Headquarters, the Taiyuan Public Security Bureau, and the Taiyuan General Chamber of Commerce should jointly organize a Foreign Exchange Inspection Committee to conduct inspections in various ways. Yesterday, an order was issued for the immediate start of inspections of various foreign exchange institutions. The document stated: "Recently, the value of provincial notes has fallen sharply, and foreign exchange rates have risen sharply, which has a great impact on the city's finances. After careful consideration, the cause is that merchants and residents are remitting foreign exchange without any restrictions, leading to this situation. Inspections should be carried out immediately to prevent disruption. It has been decided that the Finance Department, the Industry and Commerce Department, the Jin-Cha-Sui Gendarmerie Headquarters, the Taiyuan Public Security Bureau, and the Taiyuan General Chamber of Commerce should jointly organize a Foreign Exchange Inspection Committee to conduct strict inspections. In addition to separate orders, a copy of the agreed-upon rules is attached for your compliance. The Finance Department should convene and establish a committee to report for the record and quickly begin inspections." The following are the rules for inspecting foreign exchange: (1) The Foreign Exchange Inspection Committee shall be organized by the following agencies: 1. Finance Department, 2. Industry and Commerce Department, 3. Gendarmerie Headquarters, 4. Public Security Bureau, 5. General Chamber of Commerce. (2) All foreign exchange remittances must be inspected by the committee and stamped with approval. The stamp must be signed by the five agencies in the preceding article separately to ensure verification. (3) Those who remit foreign exchange without inspection and approval by the committee will have their entire amount confiscated and the remitter and the remitting merchant will be punished for violating the order. (4) These rules shall take effect from the date of promulgation. (May 29th)

Songjiang 59

Shenxiang Town Robbed by Bandits: Shenxiang Town, located in the 34th Tu of the 43rd Bao of the Tianma Mountain area in the county, is a small town near the Huating River, bordering Qingpu County. Accused of Falsehood, Wronged to Death by Poison: Wang Cao, wife of Wang Jinzhang of Pujiang, East Suburb, has recently been falsely insulted by her neighbor Chu Guo in foul language, and even assaulted and harassed. On Dragon Boat Festival, Cao went to Minhang on business, and Chu Guo again slandered Wang Jinzhang, falsely accusing his wife of having an affair with Xie Ruisheng, and going to Minhang for a secret tryst. Wang investigated and found that Xie had never left the town. It was clearly malicious slander. When Wang Cao returned home, Chu Guo followed her and openly insulted her. Cao, unable to endure it, swallowed opium in grievance and died. Her husband discovered it but it was too late to treat her. He was grief-stricken and appealed to the county government for redress to comfort her soul.

Suzhou 62

Dry Tai Cheng Robbery Case Judgement: The Dry Tai Cheng Timber Firm located at Date Market Street outside Xu Gate was robbed in March. The principal offenders, Wei Zhihe and Guo Desheng, were successively apprehended and handed over to the Wu County Local Court for trial. The verdict was delivered yesterday, sentencing Wei Zhihe to eight years and two months of imprisonment and Guo Desheng to five years and six months of imprisonment. Guo declared in court that he disagreed and would appeal to the High Court.

Li-Cheng Mutual Lawsuit Opening Before the trial began, the case of mutual accusations between State Premier Li Genyuan and his third concubine, Cheng Peiyi, had already been judged by the local court, which found Li Genyuan not guilty and Cheng Peiyi guilty of defamation, fined fifteen yuan. Cheng disagreed and filed an appeal. The trial was scheduled to open this afternoon (the 6th) at 2:00 PM.

The Third Prison Experiences Three Jail Riots: The detention center attached to the High Court in Simaqian Street is located in the Third Prison and holds over 500 inmates, mostly those involved in counter-revolutionary cases. Incidents often occur. Chief Judge Lin of the High Court recently received an anonymous letter stating that contraband was being smuggled into the facility. Yesterday (the 4th) at 10:00 AM, Prosecutor Jin Henian, together with Shi Zechen, the director of the prison department of the court, led police to search each cell in the detention center, but found nothing. They then removed unsanitary food and unauthorized chairs, tables, etc., from various cells in the First and Second Prisons. In the afternoon, Prosecutor Zhu Wenzhuo was dispatched to continue the search. A small amount of smoking paraphernalia and opium was found under the floor in the storage room of the Second Prison, and one tael of opium was found in the brick crevices under the toilet in cell 26 of the Second Prison. Since no one claimed ownership of the smoking paraphernalia and opium, Supervising Officer Zhu and the prison officials transferred Mao Yulong and two other guards on duty that day to the local court for investigation. Today (the 5th), they were planning to inspect the Third Prison, the Cross Prison, and the Infirmary, and to redistribute the inmates, moving the sick inmates to the medical facilities for better management. Unexpectedly, at 6:30 AM, the prison opened the cells for morning face washing as usual. As soon as cells one and two in the First Prison were opened, the inmates in those two cells suddenly refused to be locked up again and incited all the inmates to clamor and make demands. Led by Du Junchen, Wang Baoyu, and Wang Baowang in cell 18, they reached through the small food-delivery door and destroyed the iron locks on the cells, rushing out en masse and attempting to break through the main iron gate outside. Throwing bowls and yelling, all the inmates joined in the uproar. The situation was extremely turbulent. At the beginning of the riot, the guard on duty, Cao Yuantian, reported to the prison director. In addition to Chief Judge Lin of the High Court, Chief Prosecutor Wang, Director Shi, and Chief Secretary Wei, who arrived at the scene after hearing the news, Superintendent Ding Lei of the Public Security Bureau, the leaders of the detective and technical teams, Chief Jiang of the West District Mobile Patrol, patrol officers from various branches, and Captain Ding of the First Platoon of the Police Brigade also rushed to the scene with their squads to suppress the riot, finally bringing it under control. By 7:00 AM, the ringleaders, including Du Junchen and 26 others, had been identified and placed in shackles. The situation was finally brought under control, and the investigation is still underway.

Wuxi 63

A Violent Crime Outside West Gate: At 8:30 PM on the 4th, four thugs wearing cyan military uniforms and speaking with northern accents arrived at the Hua Songlin family's residence under the suspension bridge outside the West Gate. They knocked on the door and claimed they wanted to smoke opium. Songlin told them that he had not been selling it for a long time and asked for their understanding. The thugs then said they wanted money. As Songlin hesitated, they immediately drew sharp blades and stabbed him repeatedly, causing him to fall to the ground in a pool of blood with serious injuries. The thugs then fled westward. At the time, Songlin's father, Yongqing, was in the inner room. Hearing the commotion, he shouted for help and rushed out to chase after them, alarming the neighbors who joined in the pursuit and threw stones. In the confusion, the thugs left behind a cyan military cap with a white edge, adorned with a porcelain blue sky with a white sun emblem. The neighbors picked it up and reported it to the Public Security Bureau, requesting the arrest of the perpetrators. Songlin was carried to the Labor Hospital for treatment, fearing for his life.

Xiaoqingshan Temple Robbed: On the morning of the day before yesterday, at around 1:00 AM, seven or eight bandits suddenly appeared at Xiaoqingshan Temple in Shaotang Camp, Guanan Township, under the jurisdiction of the county. All were wearing short blue cloth shirts and trousers, carrying handguns, foreign knives, flashlights, iron bars, and the like. They opened the main gate of Qingshan Temple, and all the monks heard the alarm and fled. The bandits searched the abbot Zhengde's meditation room, stealing thirty yuan in silver and injuring the abbot's head, causing blood to flow uncontrollably. He was hired a boat to be sent to the city hospital for treatment yesterday.

County Court Set to Open: Due to the unsettled address for the construction of the county court in Xiyi, progress has been slow. The provincial government has ordered the county to expedite the eviction of the County Public Security Bureau in order to actively prepare. The Public Security Bureau has also decided to relocate to the old Xiyi Temple and has hired workers to repair it, with completion targeted for the 20th, so that they can move in immediately. It is reported that the County Court will formally open on July 1st.

Silk Cocoon Industry Faces Shortage Panic: China has always been a major exporter of raw silk. The national silk industry requires approximately 300,000 dan of dried cocoons each year. This year, the spring cocoon harvests in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces are only about 50-60% of normal. The combined dried cocoon harvest from the counties of Xiwu, Yili, Lijin, and Dan are no more than 60,000 dan. According to the production of various regions, the dried cocoons collected by the silk factories in Xidi this season are only sufficient for three months. The raw material shortage has caused a great panic in the factories. The only hope is that the summer and autumn harvests will be good, which may provide some compensation.

Wounded Soldiers Arrive in Wuxi Yesterday: The county government previously received a telegram from the Ministry of Military Affairs ordering that a portion of the wounded soldiers from the front lines be transported to Wuxi for treatment and instructing them to find suitable housing to accommodate over a thousand people. County Chief Sun dispatched Gu Yonggeng, the director of general affairs, together with the Public Security Bureau, to locate the Dongyue Temple in Huishan, the Zhangzhong Temple, and the Wang Wenzheng Ancestral Hall as locations for the rear hospital. Letters were sent to various businesses and local gentry and wealthy individuals to discuss fundraising today to provide accommodations and to request the medical association to select medical personnel to assist in treatment and recruit nurses. The wounded soldiers arrived in Wuxi from Beijing yesterday morning, numbering about one thousand. The county government and the Police Brigade of the Public Security Bureau received them at the station and escorted them to the Zhuan Mountain for settlement.

Changzhou 64

Second Day of Budget Conference: The Wuyi County 19th Fiscal Year budget conference continued on the morning of the 4th with a review session, followed by a general meeting in the afternoon. The key resolutions are recorded below: (1) Police uniform budget: The original budget of 2,500 yuan was reduced to 1,000 yuan by the review committee. County Chief Wu proposed a reconsideration, and the original amount of 2,500 yuan was reinstated. (2) County Chief Wu proposed expanding the firearms expenditure due to practical needs and requested that the original 5,000 yuan be retained. The proposal was passed. (3) District Chief He Naiyang and others proposed that the 10,000 yuan for construction projects be deleted and converted into funds for township offices. There were also proposals to convert it into educational funds. It was resolved that the matter would be submitted to the provincial authorities for approval by the county government's finance bureau. Pending approval, the funds would continue to be disbursed by the Construction Bureau. (4) It was resolved to increase the education budget by 2,000 yuan and the public security budget by 2,400 yuan. (5) It was resolved to add 1,080 yuan to the Construction Bureau for temporary expenses and delete other resolutions. Details of other resolutions omitted.

Jiangyin 65

Examination of a Standing Male Corpse in the River: The nameless male corpse found standing in the river was examined by Judge Yang Cheng yesterday. The deceased's hands and feet were tied with ropes. There were gunshot wounds in the left buttock and left posterior rib, both hitting vital areas, with the bullets remaining inside. The examination was completed and reported back to the city.

White Powder Sent to Shanghai for Testing: In the case of the Hong Wan pills in Zhangqing Township, since Detective Captain Huang Bingzhong has not been apprehended, the county bureau has reported the handling of the Hong Wan pills to the Provincial Government, the Department of Civil Affairs, and the High Court. Yesterday, the seized white powder was formally sent to the Shanghai Municipal Government for forwarding to a hospital for testing.

Bandits as Numerous as Hairs in Jiangyin: The Wu Peilang family in Xiaoyangjia Village, east of Jiangyin, was robbed by seven or eight bandits the night before last, losing sixty yuan. Zhang Heshang in Qianhuayuantou was stabbed in the leg because he had no money. The Liu Zigeng family in Liujia Village had their daughter-in-law dragged naked from the bed and thirty yuan stolen. The Wang family in Diqiao in the Sixth District was also robbed clean.

Nantong 66

Preparation for Establishing a Rear Hospital: The General Headquarters telegraphed the county government to arrange a location near the county seat to accommodate more than a thousand people for the establishment of a rear hospital. Various sectors telegraphed requesting selection of another county but was disapproved. County Chief Zhang then consulted with local sectors to select empty rooms near Langshan Mountain and prepared everything.

Local Finances Exhausted to Relief: Local finances in Tongyi have been greatly strained recently due to repeated bandit disturbances and insufficient revenue, making it impossible to make up the deficit. The County Public Funds and Property Management Office convened a meeting to discuss relief measures. It was resolved to encourage the raising of 50,000 yuan in local loans, secured by local surcharges, to be repaid in six months, and submitted to the county for forwarding to the province for approval.

Troops Stationed in Jinsha Engage Local Bandits: Troops stationed in Jinsha discovered a large gang of local bandits in the eastern countryside. They immediately intercepted them, and the bandits, unable to resist, retreated. Twelve were captured, three of whom were killed on the spot.

Zhenjiang 67

Suicide Case at Jintai Inn: At around 3:00 PM yesterday (the 4th), a man wearing a police uniform arrived at the Jintai small inn at the intersection of Zhenjiang Shaanxiang and Wanhelou Alley, carrying two pieces of luggage. He checked into room number two. After drawing water and washing his face, he unexpectedly stabbed himself violently in the abdomen and slashed his neck with a bayonet, causing his esophagus to protrude, his abdomen to rupture, his intestines to spill out, and blood to flow everywhere. The inn's tea server noticed and went out to report, but at this time the guest had not yet died. He climbed out of the door onto the drying platform and then onto the roof, from which he fell into the street and died. The police who arrived on the scene carried him back into the inn, reported to the local court for examination, and inspected his luggage. It was found that the guest's name was Liu Yongsheng, from Anfeng, Xinghua County, currently serving as a first-class police officer in the Second Squad of the Third Branch of the Gaochun County Police. Because he received a letter from his wife urging him to return home, he requested a three-week leave from the squad to return to his village. The reason for his suicide while passing through Zhenjiang is unknown.

Inmate Escapes from Court Detention Center: At midnight last night, a theft suspect escaped from the Zhenjiang Court Detention Center. Fortunately, the detention center staff discovered it during an inspection of the remaining inmates. They immediately reported to the warden, who investigated and found that the escapee had dug a hole in the cell and climbed over the courtyard wall. The escape situation has been reported to the chief judge for a wanted notice.

National Arts Branch Continues New Student Exams: The provincial National Arts Institute's affiliated Normal Training School has admitted students, and their rankings were recorded in yesterday's newspaper. It is learned that the institute is still allowing candidates from various county governments and water police teams who have been sent from afar to take exams on arrival. The previous two days saw additional supplementary exams with five new students admitted: Xia Zhonglin, Liu Mingding, Li Liansheng, Zhang Fusheng, and Lin Fei. Classes are scheduled to begin today (the 5th).

Yangzhou 68

The Truth About the Robbery in the Northwest Countryside: A gang of more than ten local bandits speaking with Qinghuaikou accents suddenly appeared in the Erli An area, northwest of this county, the night before last. Their heads and waists were wrapped in white cloth, and they each carried guns. They robbed stores including Jiuchangheng, Buyuanmao, Buyuanshun, Yichangxiang, and Wanyuan, with losses estimated at over a thousand yuan. At 12:00 PM that night, they robbed the Li Jia Zui area. The bandits changed to red cloth head coverings and went to rob Li Fuliang's house, with losses estimated at several dozen yuan. They went to Xue's house to rob. Xue Qicheng opened the door to escape and was shot in the throat and Xue Qigao was shot in the head and Xue Wenhan shot in the abdomen. When the locals heard the news and sounded the gong for help, the bandits, seeing the situation was not good, fled.

Gaoyou 69

Chief of the Second Branch Flees in Fear of Punishment: Li Zuomin, chief of the Second Branch of the Public Security Bureau in Jieshou Town under the jurisdiction of the county, has been lawless since taking office, causing the people of the town to hate him. Some people had previously filed a lawsuit against him in the county government, and a detective had been assigned to investigate and found it to be true. Li learned of this and has now abandoned his post and fled in fear of punishment. Guo Baoheng has been appointed by the general bureau to take over the vacant position.

Former Leader of the Militia Accused, Thorough Investigation Ordered: Zhang Zhaoying and others, citizens of the Seventh District under the jurisdiction of the county, are currently accusing Li Wenrong, the former leader of the militia in the district, of failing to hand over the district's firearms, intending to embezzle them, and using the excuse of procuring firearms to collect donations from the people. They have jointly filed a lawsuit with the county government requesting legal action. It is learned that the county government has dispatched someone to conduct a thorough investigation.

Yancheng 70

Bandits Rampant in Western Yancheng: On May 1st, Sheyang Town, on the border of Yancheng and Bao, was looted by bandits, with twenty-three people abducted. The next day, they robbed the Sha Jiazhuang area and kidnapped three hostages, who have not been ransomed to this day. On the 23rd of the same month, police teams from various counties and local self-defense militias gathered at Jianhekou to suppress the bandits, but the bandits had already heard the news and fled. Only a few houses of the You family (bandit hideout) were burned. Unexpectedly, on the night of the 26th, bandits suddenly arrived at Xia Huangshe and kidnapped Ling Zhongliang. At 4:00 PM on the 29th, Zhao Guansan (a local gentry director) was shot and killed, and two steel rifles were taken. At the same time, the Zhao Zhuang elementary school and neighboring houses were set on fire, Zhao Guangwen was killed, and about ten wealthy households in Jianhekou, including Su Chunyang, Ji Guandou, and Chen Zhaowei, were abducted. All public and private firearms were seized. The next day, the bandits returned to the Ling family at midnight, ordering them to prepare lunch for them the next day to await the payment of ransom. After repeated pleadings from the old farmers, it was agreed that the money would be paid on the 6th. After the meal, they went along the river to Liu Huangshe and confiscated all the self-defense guns and ammunition from the Liu family. They even threatened that anyone with guns should hand them over quickly, or they would kill and set fires. It is said that the area is now nine empty houses out of ten. The wheat is yellow and the rice seedlings are flourishing, but no one is planting or harvesting. Traffic and communication are completely cut off. This tragic situation is truly unbearable to contemplate.

Pinghu 71

Tu Danran Drowns Himself: Tu Danran, from Xubu Bridge outside the West Gate of this city, was 21 years old and enjoyed sports, often lingering around the basketball court. His father, Gengming, was over fifty years old and had three sons and one daughter, with the eldest daughter not yet married. The second son was Danran. This spring, he married a Miss Guan in the same industry through a matchmaker. Since their marriage, the couple had not been on good terms. His father had been running the Wanyuan Rice Shop for many years, and the business was still thriving. After Danran's marriage in March, his father's restrictions were very strict, and he did not have freedom in spending money, resulting in debts of about 200 yuan. During the Dragon Boat Festival, he asked his father to acknowledge the debt, but his request was not granted. On the 30th of last month, he borrowed 18 yuan from the Wanyuan accounting office and suddenly disappeared. His father, upon learning of this, asked people to search in many ways, but without result. On the 2nd, two letters were suddenly sent from the Weixin Agency on Er Ma Road in Shanghai: (1) To his family, stating that he had used up the household funds, so he had gone to Shanghai to seek a living in the Huangpu River, asking his parents not to grieve in vain; (2) To his friend's family. After receiving the letters, the family took a boat to Shanghai that night to search for him, but he was not at the Weixin Agency, so they placed an advertisement in the newspaper. Unexpectedly, Danran took the Shanghai-Hangzhou train back to Jiaxing on the 3rd. At 7:00 AM on the 4th, he took the Changshun boat to Jia Ping. When the boat reached near Jiuli Pavilion, Danran knew that the boat was about to arrive in Pinghu and he was ashamed to face his parents, so he had an anti-life idea, and pretended to urinate, jumped into the river, by the time the sailors realized to stop the boat and started searching for him, it was no longer possible to rescue him. After the boat returned to Pinghu, the boat company reported to the family, who hired a boat to salvage the body. The body has now been recovered and carried home. The family is crying. A telegram has been sent to Shanghai urging his father to return to Pinghu to handle the funeral arrangements.

Ningbo 72

Accounts After the Closure of Geng Yu Zhuang: The failure of Ningbo City's Geng Yu Money Shop was due to shareholder He Lianxing's speculative failures, resulting in the absconding of funds, leading to the closure of the shop. The total receipts and payments were approximately 800,000 yuan. After auditing by fellow money shop operators, Geng Yu Zhuang had a total loss of twelve yuan in addition to the receipts and payments. Since the shop still held five shares in Hong Cangting, the expected settlement is approximately 70% of the account.

Buddhist Temple Robbed: At the Houan Temple near Shiqiao Village in Fenghua Qin Xiao District, an old monk and a female guardian lived. The woman had forty-seven silver dollars stored away. Bandits learned of this and two bandits came one evening and robbed the money from the woman's bedroom. After the incident, the woman repeatedly tried to commit suicide, but the monk dissuaded her.

Shaoxing 73

Xiaoshan Silk Factory Searches for Bandits: After the shutdown of the Qingyun Silk Reeling Factory in Zhuan Ba Tou, Xiaoshan, the personnel dispersed, and bandits occupied it and hid weapons. Yesterday, the provincial government dispatched a special task force of more than one hundred soldiers to Xiaoshan on the afternoon of the 3rd. The Shaoxing Public Security Bureau was also ordered to send twenty patrol officers and twenty detectives, who also departed at the same time and arrived in Xiaoshan to coordinate the operation. On the morning of the 4th, they surrounded the factory in Zhuan Ba Tou and entered to search. The bandits had already heard the news and fled. Only six were captured on the spot and sent to Hangzhou for interrogation.

Deadline to Widen Daqing Street: The section of Da Jiang Bridge to Qingdao Bridge is a prosperous commercial district in the city. For the convenience of traffic and the construction of roads, the Construction Bureau has surveyed and submitted the entire section for approval to demolish and rebuild, setting the width according to regulations and marking the boundary lines for buildings along the street to be reduced. The demolition and rebuilding must be completed by the end of June. For those who fail to start construction by the deadline, the Construction Bureau, together with the fire brigade, will hire workers to demolish the buildings, and the wages will be borne by the property owners. One day before the demolition work begins, the current tenants will advance half of the payment, and the balance will be paid after the completion of the project. Those who obstruct the demolition or fail to pay wages will be sealed off to serve as a warning. This plan was submitted by the bureau at the county government meeting on the 5th and will be implemented once decided.

Shangyu 74

School Building Collapses, Injuring Five: At around 2:00 PM on the 2nd, three flat rooms of the first-grade classroom next to the gatehouse of Xiaoyue County Fourth Elementary School suddenly collapsed with a thunderous sound. Fortunately, most of the students (over sixty in the entire classroom) were resting outside after class, avoiding a major disaster. Three students, including Chen Zimiao, were unable to escape and suffered serious injuries, falling unconscious. At the same time, the gatekeeper Yao Zhaozhu and the school employee Yao A Ting were also affected. After being carried out, they were covered in blood and sent to the local hospital for treatment. Their lives are feared to be in danger. The school was originally the Yubei Second School, and was recently upgraded. The old school buildings are no longer sufficient to accommodate the increasing number of students. The current principal, Lin Chengsen, had previously planned to rebuild the school, but the estimated cost of the entire project was no less than 15,000 yuan. Zhang Jingxu, the county chief, Che Meixuan, the education director, and local gentry Wang Jili and 26 others had initiated fundraising. Unexpectedly, disaster struck.

Hefei 75

Feng Lehe Town Completely Robbed: On the 31st, at daybreak, about 200 bandits suddenly arrived at Feng Lehe Town, about seventy miles from the city in the southern countryside. They robbed all the households in the town, more than a hundred in total, without leaving anything behind. At 1:00 PM, they bundled up the stolen goods and kidnapped dozens of people, fleeing westward. Before leaving, they set fire to the houses, causing significant damage.

Dispatch Artillery Team to Assist in Suppressing Bandits: More than 1,000 bandits under the command of Quan Guangyi are currently rampant in the vicinity of Shannan Guan Town, which borders the three counties of He, Liu, and Shu. The Pan Regiment from Lu'an has already been dispatched and a letter has been sent to Hefei requesting a team to assist in the suppression. County Chief Wang, due to the urgent need for city defense, was unable to leave, and dispatched mortar team leader Wang Shencheng with four mortars on the 1st to assist in the suppression.

Chinese Team Returns to Shanghai This Morning from Eastern Expedition 76

Ryota Maru Expected to Arrive at Huishan Wharf at 9:00 AM

Sports Advancement Association and Various Sectors Prepare to Welcome

The Ninth Far Eastern Games have concluded. The Chinese athletes departed from Tokyo on the 1st, touring Yokohama and other places before returning home. The Chinese baseball team, along with overseas Chinese from Honolulu, returned directly to their hometowns. Athletes from the Northeast and Tianjin took the route via Busan, South Korea. The rest of the team will return to Shanghai aboard the Ryota Maru, expected to arrive at Huishan Wharf at approximately 9:00 AM this morning. The Sports Advancement Association, various organizations, and relatives and friends of the athletes will prepare to welcome them. Beiping Zhongda Basketball Team Wins 77

Defeats Datong by a Score of 36 to 16 Last Night

The Beiping China University basketball team competed against the Datong University basketball team at the China Basketball Hall at 8:00 PM last night. Referee Li Jiyuan's final score was 36 to 16, with Beiping China University winning. The first half score was 18 to 12 in favor of Beiping China University. Yesterday was the first time the entire team of Beiping China University displayed their skills. With their height and strength, they were quite capable of representing the athletes of the North. However, their teamwork was not yet well-honed. Although they won because the opponent was of average strength, the performance of the team did not excite the audience. They will face the Xiaoxing team at 8:00 PM tonight. The Xiaoxing team has many talented players and is capable of competing with China University.

As the battle unfolded, China University came down hard, with a fierce attitude. Datong panicked and fell into disarray. China University easily scored four consecutive points. Datong called for a time out to reorganize. After a short time, the defense was gradually reinforced, and China University was unable to do as they pleased. The situation leveled out. In the first half, China University took the lead with a score of 18 to 12. Switching sides and battling again, Datong once again fell into disarray. China University took advantage of the situation to attack and was invincible, resulting in China University winning with a score of 36 to 16.

Detailed Report on the 9th Far Eastern Games (7)

Tragedy of the Sino-Japanese Football Final 80

Referee's Unjust Bias Provokes Universal Derision

Three-Three Draw, Championship Retained

(Tokyo Dispatch) In this football tournament, Japan first defeated the Philippines by a score of seven to five, creating a great stir. Subsequently, our nation also defeated the Philippines by five to zero, forming a confrontational situation. On the 29th, at 3 p.m., the Sino-Japanese football final was held at the Meiji Jingu Stadium. Nearly ten thousand spectators were in attendance. Our cheering squad, dressed in red hats and white uniforms, waved flags and cheered, filled with vigor. Unexpectedly, the referee, Takeuchi Toraji, possessed no sporting spirit or sense of fair play, arbitrarily favoring Japan. He unreasonably penalized our players, using offside as a hindrance to our team's offensive, our only weapon. Spectators, aside from the Japanese, were filled with indignation. However, our team members remained calm and fought valiantly, ultimately achieving a three-three draw, no easy feat. The details of the battle are as follows:

Referee Policy　 The Japanese side utilized the referee's bias in various ball games. At the beginning of the match, they strictly targeted the opposing athletes, causing them to lose their spirit. Then, the Japanese army took the opportunity to attack. The same was true for the football match on this day. Within the first fifteen minutes, whenever our team's forwards received the ball and broke through the Japanese team's inner defense line, the referee would blow his whistle loudly, shouting "Offside!" It was both infuriating and ridiculous. As a result, our offense was unable to advance and had to retreat. In the twenty-fifth minute, the Japanese center forward, Shiro Teshima, scored a goal, putting our team in an increasingly disadvantageous position. The ball hovered in front of our goal, but fortunately, goalkeeper Zhou Xianyuan defended well, otherwise, who knows how many more goals we would have lost.

Draw Achieved　 Afterwards, our team was penalized for offside several times. Fortunately, our soldiers fought bravely. Captain Sun Jinshun, fearless, single-handedly broke through the enemy's line. Finally, in the thirty-seventh minute, he kicked a goal from the right, achieving a tie. The Japanese referee policy had to temporarily admit defeat. The first half ended with a score of one to one, a draw. Most memorably, our team was penalized for offside seven times in the first half, while the Japanese team was not penalized even once.

Twelve Minutes　 After switching sides, our team faced an unfavorable headwind. Within three minutes, we were penalized for two corner kicks, creating a very dangerous situation. In the twelfth minute, the Japanese forwards swarmed forward again, and center forward Teshima scored another goal, making the score one to two, Japan leading. Seeing the dangerous situation, our team quickly adjusted its troops, replacing Chen Jiaqiu with Ye Beihua and Li Ning with Feng Yunyou. After the reinforcements entered the field, our team's formation was immediately invigorated. In the sixteenth minute, center forward Dai Linjing dribbled the ball straight towards the enemy goal, raised his foot slightly, and the ball entered the net, making the score two to two, another draw.

Unjust Penalty　 In the twenty-third minute, the Japanese team's right wing, Takayama, received the ball and advanced straight forward. Liang Xianzhan quickly went to intercept it, but the referee suddenly blew his whistle loudly, declaring a foul and awarding a twelve-yard penalty kick. The spectators were all worried for our team, but the ball went over the crossbar, a lucky outcome.

Score Equal Again　 In the twenty-eighth minute, the Japanese team launched another attack. Right forward Shinoshima scored a goal at the edge of the goal, and Zhou Xianyuan was unable to save it, making the score two to three, Japan leading again. Fortunately, in the thirty-fifth minute, Chen Xianyao received the ball and dribbled straight forward, then passed it to Sun Jinshun. Sun passed it to Chen Jiaqiu in front of the goal, and Chen passed it to Dai Linjing. Dai turned around and kicked the ball into the net with all his might, making the score three to three, another tie.

Final Melee　 Afterwards, both sides fought hard for the final five minutes. Our army's momentum increased, and the entire army pressed towards the enemy. There were five opportunities to score, but none were successful, which was a great pity. Most regrettably, Sun Jinshun received the ball in front of the goal, and the Japanese goalkeeper rushed out to grab it but failed. Sun panicked slightly, raised his right foot, and the ball went too far to the right, going out of bounds. Secondly, Dai Linjing shot from about ten steps from the goal, but it was slightly too high, and the ball did not enter the net, which was extremely unfortunate. Before long, the silver whistle sounded, and the ball game ended with a score of three to three.

Game Stopped　 According to football rules, if both teams are tied, the game should be extended for twenty minutes. However, the Japanese referee declared that the game would stop today and be rescheduled for another day. Our team was in uproar. The coach reported to the head coach, John Ma, and formally protested, arguing that the referee had no right to overturn the football rules. The Japanese side was at a loss for words. At 7 p.m. that evening, the committee was convened, and both sides debated for a long time. It was decided that the football game would not be played again, and the championship would be retained until the next tournament. Our chief representative, Zhang Boling, strongly disagreed and insisted on continuing the game. After convening a meeting of officials, it was recognized that the Japanese referee's actions were unreasonable and that continuing the game would bring more harm than good, so it was decided not to play.

Public Outrage of Overseas Chinese　 On this day, no less than a thousand members of the cheering squad and overseas Chinese watched the game. Seeing the Japanese referee's unreasonable oppression, they were filled with public outrage. After the game, they gathered at the athletics field and refused to disperse. They elected three representatives to meet with Hao Boyang, requesting the sports association to formally negotiate with the Japanese side. If there were no results, they should request to withdraw from the Far Eastern Games. After Hao repeatedly comforted them, they finally dispersed.

Goto, Takeuchi, Nozawa, Takekoshi, Honda, Takayama, Shinoshima, Teshima, Wakabayashi (Ishibashi), Haruyama

Chinese Basketball Team Loses to Japan Again for the Second Time

Result: Twenty-One to Thirty-Seven 81

Extreme Unfairness of the Referee　　 (Tokyo Dispatch) Our country's second basketball game against Japan was held on the evening of the 27th. Due to rain, it was moved to the indoor gymnasium of Tokyo Prefectural First Middle School. Because the Japanese officials of the Far Eastern Games had not negotiated with the Metropolitan Police Department in advance, it took a lot of trouble to get permission for the game to start at 9 p.m.

In the first half, our country started with Tang Baokun and Yao Enhan as forwards, Jian Chang as center, and Lu Guanjun and Lu Zhongen as guards. Less than a minute after the start, Japan's Ohashi scored a goal, opening the scoring. After a minute and a half, Lu Zhongen scored a free throw, making the score two to one. After that, the two sides fought hard. Japan repeatedly tried to attack but failed. After five minutes, Kobayashi, the newly substituted center, scored a goal, making the score six to one. Before long, the Japanese forwards continued to score, reaching a large difference of fourteen to one. In the fourteenth minute, Liu Jianchang scored two consecutive goals. At the end of the first half, the result was twenty-one to eleven, with China losing by ten points.

In the second half, our team replaced Tang Baokun with Chen Shengkui, Liu Jianchang with Wang Yuzeng, and Liu Guanjun with Wei Pengyun. After the start, Japan scored a goal first. Then, our team's Chen Shengkui and Yao Enhan also scored. At this time, our team's momentum turned strong, and we repeatedly got opportunities to shoot, but none were successful. Especially Wang Yuzeng missed many opportunities. Our country worked hard to catch up, making the score twenty-three to nineteen, a difference of only two points. However, the Japanese side did not show weakness. Ohashi and Tanaka continued to attack effectively, and the score suddenly increased to twenty-nine to nineteen. Seeing the Japanese team's arrogance increasing, our army immediately ordered a change of line. The players who entered the field next were Tang Baokun and Wei Pengyun as forwards, Liu Jianchang as center, and Li Guochen and Wang Xiliang as guards. After that, both sides scored, but our team saw that the general situation was going to be lost and worked even harder, but the formation became chaotic. Finally, Liu Jianchang was sent off, and our team could do nothing more. The overall result was thirty-seven to twenty-one, with our team losing by sixteen points. Our team's performance on this evening was not bad. The defense seemed to be slightly tighter than the previous game against Japan, but Tang Baokun did not get the chance to move around, and the players' poor shooting accuracy were the two main reasons for the failure.

Intense Second Game Between China and the Philippines in Basketball 82

China Loses Again with a Score of Forty-Three to Forty-Eight

Extremely Chaotic Formation with No Coordination or Tactics

(Tokyo Dispatch) At 7:30 p.m. on the 28th, the second basketball game between China and the Philippines took place. This was the last chance for the Chinese team. The audience was not very crowded, and few Chinese cheerleaders came to the stadium to cheer them on. This was because of the repeated failures of the Chinese team, which reduced the interest of the supporters. In terms of technique, our team had indeed regressed compared to what they showed in the country. Slow coordination and inaccurate shots were the biggest problems. The percentage of shots made was only about 30% on average, meaning only three out of ten shots were made. The average percentage for the Philippines and Japan was about 60-70%, so how could China not lose? The game this evening was especially laughable. In the first half, everyone except Tang Baokun was not in the formal lineup, but they were still able to win with a score of 30 to 15. In the second half, everyone except Lu Zhongen, who was taken out four times, and Liu Guanjun in the inner defense were in the formal lineup, but they were defeated by a score of 13 to 33. Isn't that strange? The referee this evening was very fair, and the Chinese soldiers were to blame.

Chen Shengkui Scores a Goal At the beginning of the game, Wang Yuzeng made a 0-point shot. Tang Baokun got the ball and passed it to Chen Shengkui. Before long, the ball was snatched away by the Filipino army. The battle became more intense after four minutes. Suddenly, the Filipino forward, Filonino, dribbled the ball straight in, as fast as an arrow. The inner defense couldn't stop it, and the ball went into the basket, opening the scoring. Our team became more determined to resist the violence. Chen Shengkui started shooting and made two consecutive shots. Tang Baokun also made a shot from the center line, making the score 6 to 2, China winning. So the morale was boosted. Both sides were in a melee, and there was no cooperation or rules. They just threw the ball when they got it. Tang Baokun made as many as nine shots. The Filipino army collapsed and was at a loss everywhere. But in this battle, the field was smoky and chaotic, and the shadows were rolling. Both sides were just wielding their clubs in a rude and far-fetched way. Our inner guard, Lu Zhongen, took the ball and dribbled it desperately, never talking about passing. There were no tactics to speak of, but the first half was actually able to win by a large margin of 30 to 15. How strange!

Closing Ceremony of the Games Prince Chichibu Gives Awards Filipino Army Launches a Major Counterattack After the break, the Filipino army changed sides and adopted a long-range shooting strategy. At that time, our side replaced Chen Shengkui with Yao Enhan, but they couldn't resist the Filipino army's attack. Tang Baokun was fouled three times and didn't dare to move. If he could have calmed down and waited for the opportunity, he wouldn't have failed. Unexpectedly, all the soldiers were flustered and still attacking the enemy in a mess, which allowed the Filipino army to take advantage of the situation. The record changed from 42 to 36 to 42 to 38 to 42 to 42. After the scores were averaged, the Filipino army became even braver and our army became even more chaotic. Li Guochen fouled again and was fouled by the Filipino army, making the score 42 to 43. Then, in two minutes, the Filipino army broke through two more goals, making the score 42 to 47. The Philippines also made one free throw. In the second half, China lost by 13 to 23, and the overall score was 48 to 43, with the Philippines winning by a large margin.

Japan therefore gained a great advantage and remained ahead of the Filipino army. By the 13th minute, the score was 33 to 27. Overall, Ms. Mudan's women's singles performance on this day was indeed very good. The advantages of being leisurely and not busy, attacking the weak and avoiding the strong are far beyond what the other party, Ms. Garia, can do. Important News Ministry of Education

Expedient Measures for Reporting Matters to Bureaus and Departments in Installments 86

The Ministry of Education issued an order to the education bureaus of each province and city regarding matters that could be reported in installments: According to the Jiangxi Provincial Department of Education, the term of office for principals and faculty in the province is mostly limited to one academic year, and it is proposed to revise the "Schedule of Matters to be Reported in Installments by Educational Administrative Organs of Each Province and City" issued by the Ministry. "The qualifications, experience, positions, salaries, full-time or part-time positions, etc. of the principals and faculty of each secondary school shall be reported once within one month after the start of each semester" shall be slightly changed to be reported once within one month after the start of each academic year. Also, in the original schedule, "The grades of graduates and students of all levels in each secondary school shall be reported once within one month after the end of each semester. The department believes that the grades of graduates of all levels are usually listed separately by subject and semester and academic year, and the scores and credits are listed in detail. As for the grades of students, it is acceptable not to report the subjects specifically, but to report the total semester scores of each student to avoid duplication. After investigation, the Ministry found that what was stated was feasible and should be slightly changed. All principals and faculty of secondary schools in each province and city whose term of office is more than one academic year may report their qualifications, experience, positions, salaries, full-time or part-time positions, etc. within one month after the start of each academic year. However, if the term of office is limited to one semester, they must still report it every semester. Also, the grades of students of all levels in secondary schools that are reported every semester may not list the subjects specifically, but report the total semester scores of each student. In addition to the instruction and distribution, the order shall be made known to all.

Ministry of Education Pays Attention to New Gansu Artifacts 87

The Ministry of Education telegraphed the governments of Xinjiang and Gansu provinces that the visit of the British Stein to New Gansu this time was of a tourist nature, and the passport issued by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs was limited to tourism only. If there is any collection of antiques or transit out of the country, it is hoped that it will be investigated and stopped at any time, and that all affiliated units will pay attention to it.

Ministry of Education Collects Educational Lantern Slides 88

The Ministry of Education, with the approval of a letter from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs regarding McGill University in Montreal, Canada, requesting lantern slides of our country's culture and education, issued a circular to its subordinate educational administrative organs. The case was approved based on an official letter from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, which stated, "According to the Consul General stationed in Canada, 'We have received a letter from McGill University in Montreal, Canada, requesting lantern slides of Chinese culture and education for research purposes. A copy of the original letter from the university is enclosed. Please forward it to the Ministry of Education to send the slides or other promotional materials directly so that we can forward them.' Accordingly, a copy of the original attached letter is enclosed for your review and action. Please reply.'" In addition to issuing separate orders, the original letter is copied and distributed, instructing you to immediately comply and compile the educational lantern slides or related promotional materials you have produced and submit them to the Ministry for forwarding. This order is issued.

Suzhou Provincial Department of Education

Order to Urge Registered Schools to Exchange for Official Seals 89

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education has issued an order to all registered private secondary schools regarding the urgent matter of exchanging seals. According to Instruction No. 1087 from the Ministry of Education, the issuance of seals for private schools at all levels has been addressed. The Ministry has drafted regulations and submitted them to the Executive Yuan, which in turn submitted them to the National Government, resulting in an official order that all seals should be uniformly issued by the competent educational administrative organs. Therefore, all registered private schools at all levels requiring seals should immediately submit requests according to their level to the respective competent educational administrative organs for issuance. The materials and dimensions should strictly comply with the regulations on seals issued by the National Government and the attached seal diagrams (square wooden seal, 5.2 cm on each side). You are instructed to inform all registered private schools at all levels accordingly. It has been a long time since the order was issued, and only a few have complied. In addition to issuing reminders, we urgently order you to instruct the principals of your schools to immediately apply for the exchange of seals in accordance with the regulations to comply with the established rules. Do not delay any further. This order is imperative.

Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education's Order for Urgency

Report on Inspection by County Supervisors and Education Committee Members 90

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education issued an instruction to the heads of education bureaus in various counties regarding the urgent matter of reporting inspections. The number of inspections by county supervisors and education committee members has long been stipulated. Each county supervisor must inspect all educational institutions in the county at least once per semester, and each education committee member must inspect the schools in their district at least three times per semester. Inspection records or reports must be submitted to the Department for review. Despite repeated reminders, the inspection reports for the first semester of the 18th year have not yet been received from your county. Such arbitrary delays are highly inappropriate. Therefore, we issue another order instructing you, the bureau chief, to immediately compile and submit the inspection reports of each member for the first semester of the 18th year within half a month of receiving this document for review and verification. Do not delay further, or you will be held accountable. This order is to be forwarded and made known.

Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education Investigation

Third Day of the Conference of County Education Bureau Chiefs 91

The third meeting of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education's conference of county education bureau chiefs was held at 8:00 AM on the fourth. Director Chen of the Department presided, with Yang Naikang acting as the recorder and Yang Changyun and Huang Rujian performing the rituals. Gao Qian gave a lecture in the morning, and Zhu Jianbai gave a lecture in the afternoon. Reporting items: 1. The Education Funding Group reported on the review situation. Discussion items: 1. Proposal to increase the land tax for education. Resolutions:

(1) Counties whose total tax revenue has not yet reached the 1% limit should follow the provincial government's published regulations for reorganizing the universal education land tax in various counties and increase the tax as much as possible to comply with the established plan. (2) The estimated land prices in each county should be determined by the province with detailed standards and procedures, and the counties should be instructed to publicly estimate the prices. The prices cannot be determined solely based on the virtual estimates of a few agency personnel. 1. Proposal to request the opening of the reed field tax for military settlements. Resolution: A special project should be carefully drafted for the universal education land tax, regardless of whether it is for grain land, reed land, salt land, or military settlements, and submitted for approval. 1. Proposal to allocate funds from the Gengzi Indemnity for free education. Resolution: This proposal is reserved. 1. Proposal to collect education tax along with the railway. Resolution: This proposal is reserved. 1. Proposal to collect education surtax on tobacco and alcohol. Resolution: This proposal is reserved. 1. Proposal to increase the salt tax. Resolution: Two cents should be allocated from the price increase of each catty of Huai salt, and the education bureaus of the respective counties should follow the original plan and coordinate to proceed. 1. Proposal to reorganize the slaughter surtax. Resolution: The Department of Education should be requested to discuss with the Education Funding Management Office to incorporate the slaughter surtax amounts of each county into the regular tax amount for unified bidding and payment of guarantee money, and to handle it jointly with the Education Bureau. 1. Proposal for the standard for the distribution of various expenses. Resolution: Unless otherwise specified in special projects, new expenses should be distributed according to the ratio of 30% for social education, 50% for compulsory education, and 20% for universal education. 1. Proposal for the investigation and compensation of arrears in education expenses. Resolution: (1) The Department of Education should be requested to formulate regulations for the reorganization of the Education Expense Committee and submit them to the provincial government meeting for discussion and promulgation. (2) The Department of Education should be requested to instruct the finance bureaus of each county through the Department of Finance to collect the old arrears of education expenses from previous years within a limited time. 1. Proposal for measures to prevent the misappropriation of education expenses. Resolution: The Department of Education should be requested to consult with the Department of Finance and instruct the finance bureaus of each county to strictly comply with previous orders and not to misappropriate funds. 1. Proposal for bookkeeping improvement and cost reduction. Resolution: The Department has already drafted and promulgated regulations, so no further discussion is needed. 1. Proposal on how to compensate for the cancellation of the 25% education fee retained for transportation. Resolution: The Department of Education should instruct the county governments to discuss solutions with the finance and education bureaus and submit them to the provincial government meeting for a decision to be followed. 1. Proposal for the standard for the distribution of school expenses. Resolution: The Department's orders should be strictly followed. 1. Proposal to stipulate the standard for the distribution of expenses for experimental primary schools and central primary schools. Resolution: The Department should be requested to issue a clear order stipulating the standards. Jin Yingyuan, the head of the Jurong County Education Bureau, proposed that a separate county education funding management office be established for local education. The chairman appointed Jin Yingyuan, Chen Da, Xu Yipeng, Yang Binru, Xiang Weixian, Wu Yaozhang, Liu Shaozhen, Jiang Zhuoqun, and Qin Fengxiang to form a review committee to review the proposal and then submit it to the general meeting for discussion.
