Qian Fengzhang to Depart for the United States Tomorrow 96

Mr. Qian Fengzhang, a graduate of the Electrical Engineering Department of Jiaotong University, initially worked as an engineer at the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications. When the National Revolutionary Army arrived in Shanghai, he was hired by the Construction Department of the former Guangxi Provincial Government to establish a wireless telecommunications enterprise. He first built the Wuzhou and Liuzhou long-wave radio stations, followed by short-wave stations. He then served as the director of the Wuzhou Wireless Radio Station and concurrently as the director of the Guangxi Wireless Machinery Manufacturing Plant. He returned north last year and resumed his position as a long-distance telephone engineer in the Construction Department of the Anhui Provincial Government. He has now been dispatched by the provincial government to investigate telecommunications and transportation in the United States and is scheduled to depart on the Empress of Russia on June 7th.

All Schools to Submit Tuition Fees by a Specified Date

The Shanghai County Education Bureau yesterday instructed the principals of all elementary schools in the county, stating, "Regarding compliance with the order, the tuition fees of each school for this semester have long been included in the budget for this year. Now that the year is coming to an end, the tuition fees collected by each school should be returned and paid in full by a specified date to complete the accounts. For students who do not meet the free tuition regulations, the tuition fees that should be paid but have not been paid, or have been paid but not cleared, should also be diligently urged by the principals of each school to pay in order to prioritize education funds. Free Talk

A Laughing Matter - Hai Ke 99

A: You're so stubborn and ignorant. Were you born in a pigsty?

B: Yes, precisely because I was born in a pigsty, I'm used to hearing pigs squeal and don't think much of it.

A (Secretly draws a large tortoise on B's back with white powder, then says to B with a smile after a while) Hey, Lao B, take off your clothes and see if that trademark was put on by yourself?

B: You're too lazy. Why didn't you just stand properly instead of leaning your back against mine, which made your shadow print on my clothes?

A: You've fallen madly in love with Miss S. I heard you spent a lot of money on her. Now that she's dumped you, do you feel the sadness of being dumped? B: Although the feeling of being dumped is uncomfortable, it's still better than never having experienced the joy of love.

A: Yes, it's always a bit better. The movie theaters, game fields, Western restaurants, silk shops, jewelry stores, etc., have all benefited from you.

Common Sense for Summer 100

·Hold· Buddha

When skin is bitten by mosquitoes or bedbugs and feels itchy, there is no need to apply floral water. Instead, wipe with soap-soaked water, which can stop itching and disinfect more effectively than floral water. The venomous liquid secreted by mosquitoes and bedbugs is called formic acid, which becomes neutral when it meets alkaline soap, thus becoming non-toxic. It's cheap and effective, why not give it a try?

After being bitten by a centipede, one can find a ground beetle (a shell-less snail) and rub it on the bitten area, which can eliminate the poison and stop the pain. It is extremely effective.

On summer nights, one is often troubled by mayflies (a type of small green insect) flying around the lamp. One can place a bowl of water, and the mayflies will fly into the water and swim around.

Rubbing hands and feet with ginger juice in the summer will prevent chilblains in the winter. Eating garlic can prevent cholera in the autumn.

After bathing, rub the whole body with a dry cloth, especially the spine, until it is red. The effect is no less than a massage, and you will feel refreshed and very happy.

Burning small candles in watermelons and lotus pods and hanging them in the courtyard on summer nights is incredibly beautiful.

ABC, Hegemon of the World 101

— Wang Yanjin

China, a First-Rate Power of the Future

My friend, Mr. Zhao Lingxian, went to study in London, England, two years ago. He lost his father in middle age and was unable to continue his studies. He suspended his studies this spring and returned to Shanghai. My teacher, Mr. Chen Minqing, and eighteen others hosted a banquet for him at the Atlantic Rong Society. The conversations were lively, and the descriptions of the lives of British women, who can be free from worrying about food and clothing in their youthful years and can indulge in the embrace of men all day long, and other customs were all very interesting. Among them, the matter of our country being a first-rate power in the future was bizarre and superstitious. I recorded it to share with readers and await confirmation in the future.

There is a Mr. Bennett in a street in London who runs a questioning stall to make a living, and it has been three years. This spring, a university professor suffered a severe mental breakdown. His wife submitted a volume to Mr. Bennett, asking him to treat him at a certain hospital. As a result, it worked, and Mr. Bennett's name became famous, and his life became more prosperous. A French missionary went to ask about the future world powers. Mr. Bennett thought for a moment and replied with emotion: In the future world, there will only be three countries: ABC. A is America, which dominates the Americas; B is Britain, which stands tall in Europe; and C is China, which is at peace in Asia. At that time, all the newspapers in London competed to publish this prediction and attributed the reasons for the strength of Britain and the United States to the fact that China's wealth and power were due to the intelligence and enlightenment of its people.

Alas, Mr. Yu Tiansui 102

— Zheng Yimei

Mr. Yu Tiansui, whose real name was Yu Shouyi, was from Yufeng. He was eccentric and self-satisfied and called himself "Crazy Lord." As a pioneer of the revolution, he assisted General Yao Yuping in his military affairs and had a spirit of "killing bandits on horseback and writing proclamations off the horse." After the success of the revolution, he retired and devoted himself to poetry and prose. He joined the Southern Society and became a leader in the literary world, unmatched. He was also skilled in writing in the chicken claw style and made monkey old man books in tadpole style, revealing a strong and vigorous spirit, which was regarded as a treasure by those who obtained it. He taught at Caoqiao Middle School in Wuzhong and Chengzhi Middle School in Shanghai for more than ten years. There were no less than hundreds or thousands of students. I also served Mr. with the etiquette of a disciple. Every time I visited or met him at a banquet, he would hold my hand and ask about my recent situation, which was more cordial than usual. He would talk to me about scholarship, and his words were exquisite and brilliant, like jade chips and orchid moss. He once said that scholarship is not easy. I have been reading for forty years before I dare to call myself a knowledgeable person. Mr. had reached the state of thorough understanding. Mr. contracted hemoptysis due to overwork and frustration. It occurred from time to time. In the winter, he was seriously ill and lingering, and he passed away at the end of the year. His illness worsened this spring, and he suddenly returned to the Tao on the 21st of the previous month. He was over fifty years old. After hearing the news, I couldn't help but shed tears. The deep feelings between teacher and student came from the depths of my being. Mr. was a man of great reputation and valued. Although he wrote a lot of works in his daily life, he discarded them as he wrote them and did not collect them himself. Those that were scattered in magazines and newspapers, I deeply hope that someone will compile them into a collection and publish them to last the world, which is also the responsibility of those who die later. Mr. had many side skills. He was skilled in music, engraving, and the art of healing. He could also paint landscapes and flowers. I have his painting of a plum blossom fan, which is elegant and extraordinary, different from the works of ordinary painters. I have treasured it and cannot bear to touch it again.

The Queen 103

Cang

A certain university professor often makes humorous remarks when he teaches. Last night, a friend told me one of the professor's remarks, which was quite interesting and valuable. I recorded it to share with readers.

The professor said that the most important social problems are food and sex. If there is food but no sex, life will inevitably be monotonous. Therefore, the pursuit of sex is universal. However, most of those who pursue it cannot get what they want. The example of the queen is like this. The so-called queen is the jade among women. One school has the queen of one school, one place has the queen of one place, one country has the queen of one country, and so on to the world, there is also the queen of the whole world. The above-mentioned queens, except for the queen of one school, whose photos are often seen in pictorials, the rest are rarely seen. The queens of one school, one place, one country, and the whole world are only one, but there are quite a few people who want to ascend the throne of emperor. As a result of the competition, victory often belongs to the beautiful or learned. It is extremely difficult for the ugly and foolish to be lucky enough to win. Therefore, those who are ugly and want to be emperors must work hard to study. There is no other way. I hope that you will not be discouraged if you fail to become emperors while you are in school. You must know that even if the throne of one school is lost, the thrones in other aspects still exist. You should work hard to study. After you have completed your studies in the future, sitting on the golden throne will be a matter of course. However, what is worrying is that the implementation of communism is a crisis for the ugly because marriage is absolutely free in communist society. It is easy for beautiful people to become emperors, but it is difficult for ugly people. Therefore, ugly people do not support communism. At this point, the students couldn't help but laugh.

Interesting Anecdotes from the Countryside 104

— Hold Buddha

People in Shaanxi attach great importance to eating fish. A friend who returned from Shaanxi said that Shaanxi is extremely high. People walking on the Qinling Mountains look down at the clouds and mists, unable to distinguish the mountains and valleys. Rain must fall under the mountains. People live in the clouds and are far away from the vast sea. There is a saying in the countryside that "Shaanxi is halfway to heaven." Shaanxi has a lot of land and few rivers. The vegetables are green onions, chives, garlic, and ginger. Every meal does not forget meat, and beef, mutton, donkey, and chicken are often served as dishes. Fresh fish is very rare and expensive. Although it is a delicacy for entertaining guests, they dare not taste it lightly. Those who are scholars and have never eaten it when they were young are afraid of its bones. When eating, they must check their eyes, correct their teeth and tongue, and still be afraid that they will not be able to spit out the bones, or assist them with their hands to take them out. They are trembling with fear, only afraid of pricking their throats. If someone happens to talk to them, they will be scolded, saying that if they are stupid, they will be chattering and not seeing that they are eating fish, how can they have time to answer each other? Another friend, Mr. Qian, once traveled to Hetao. One day, a scholar entertained him with delicacies. Looking at it, there were a few small fish and more than ten shrimp. The cooking was not done properly, and there was no freshness, but the locals praised it non-stop.

The custom in Chu is not to talk about ghosts in the morning. People in Chu have been afraid of ghosts since ancient times. Ordinary people often invite shamans to descend to the gods and worship ghosts to pray for peace and recovery if they have a disease. The life of the pipa alley is deserted, and they also burn incense to please ghosts to pray for entanglement, competing to throw money until the night is late and the moon is up. Burning paper money and paper ingots is common in every street. The heat is hateful. The custom has been followed for a long time, which is even more common than in Jiangnan. The word "ghost" is said to be the most unlucky, and they dare not say it. In the morning, expatriates from other provinces are ignorant of the taboo and accidentally say the word "ghost" and words that sound similar to "turtle", etc. When people in Chu hear it, they close their eyes, shake their heads, and cover their ears with their hands, running away quickly as if chased by evil demons and ghosts. Such superstition is ridiculous.

Visiting the Embroidery Exhibition of Qunyi Girls' School 105

— Yu Jianhua

Other than Qunyi Girls' School, there has been no public embroidery exhibition in Shanghai. Qunyi has been run independently by Ms. Guo Chunqing. For the past eight years, it has been thriving. Unfortunately, this year it was forced to move by the landlord. As it was not easy to find suitable school buildings, after repeated negotiations with the landlord, Ms. Guo, with the spirit of revolution, fought hard against the capitalists on the one hand and held an exhibition of embroidery achievements on the other hand, hoping to arouse social attention and provide assistance. Her heart is also very kind. After noon on the old Dragon Boat Festival, I went to the school on Haining Road with my younger sister to visit. Five or six students were lined up inside the gate with smiling faces, distributing special catalogs and Ms. Guo's letter of opinion with the landlord to the guests. The principal cordially entertained us and we feasted our eyes. The first room was a black line embroidery with multiple screens. The second room was a sketching embroidery with many Western paintings of landscapes and flower sketches. The third room was the works of the elementary school department, with twenty-four filial piety pictures, one for each person. The fourth room was the works of the graduates of this year. The fifth room was the practical works of each grade, mostly embroidered pillows. The sixth room was the works of alumni, with landscape screens, longevity screens, and Eight Immortals screens, etc. There were hundreds of exhibits, dazzling and beautiful. Looking at them, one can only praise them. This shows that the school is well-managed and the professors are enthusiastic, so the achievements are brilliant. I sincerely hope that Ms. Guo will uphold the spirit of struggle and fight against difficulties with unyielding perseverance. With determination, she will have a more grand exhibition next year, educating young children and seeking employment for women. Is it just the light of Qunyi School alone? After the visit, I was invited to inscribe a character. I gladly wrote the four characters "Ingenious Beyond Nature," returned, and recorded it to tell the readers.

Red Carpet

Leaving Fragrance and Sound 106

— Chongliang

If one wants to count Xun Huisheng's famous plays, one must first mention "Sister Thirteen." This is universally recognized both north and south, and is by no means a flattering word from those who are fond of the play. Apart from Yao Qing, only Huisheng can conform to the graceful and robust spirit of the female knight. Therefore, every time this play is posted in Shanghai this spring, it must be a hit. The Great China Record Company specially hired Xun Jun to record the two-six beautiful tunes of the Bow and Inkstone Edge. With the addition of Ma Fulu's painted face and Deng Jiugongyi, it feels more vivid and beautiful. Huisheng has recorded many records, but her first masterpiece, "Sister Thirteen," is still the first time it has been recorded, which is especially precious.

The farce of "Visiting Relatives and Scolding" is a comedic play known to both women and children. Yao Qing was a wonderful material for this play back then. Now, only Huisheng has the graceful and luxurious atmosphere of a noble banner lady. However, Yao Qing's voice is not suitable for recording records, so one should plan to match Huisheng with a complete 彩旦角 (female clown character) to achieve the beauty of mutual benefit. Now, apart from Ma Fulu, how many people can be called this position? Therefore, listening to the complete play of "Visiting Relatives and Scolding" sung by Xun and Ma, one feels that the comedic 京白 (Beijing dialect) and the graceful and smooth singing are enough to show the unique advantages of the play.

Today, those who perform "Cuiping Mountain" are called the brightest stars of the time, Xun Huisheng and Xiao Cuihua. However, Huisheng has a sweet voice and is good at singing, so she is actually better than Cuihua in the record. The Great China Record Company once included a section of the 南梆子 (Nan Bangzi) from her account, with the addition of a complaint-like recitation, so that it does not feel dry and monotonous. Looking around the north and south, Huisheng must be pushed as the overlord of this play.

The above three plays are all masterpieces of Huisheng, who is unrivaled in both the north and the south. When these films are released in two weeks, I dare to say that they will be extremely popular.

Warmth in My Heart 107

(207)

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter Eleven: Emerald Nets and Pearl Hairpins: Beautiful Women Return to Good Men; Green Cottages and Crimson Curtains: Famous Courtesans Marry Famous Families. At that time, Zuo Shichen hurriedly asked, "What is 'high ascension'? I don't understand." The elder aunt was a little embarrassed and said, "Second Young Master, don't pretend to be stupid. You must have heard some news outside." Zuo Shichen really didn't understand the meaning of her "high ascension" and said, "What high ascension? Why don't you explain it clearly?" The elder aunt's face turned a little red and said, "High ascension is getting married. We call it 'leaving the profession' in the hall." Zuo Shichen said, "Then, when Anan comes back later, I have to congratulate her!" Although Zuo Shichen said generous words, he couldn't help but feel a little sad when he heard this real news. He casually asked, "Which family is it?" The elder aunt said, "It's that young master Zhang. They run the Xingdang pawnshop in Shanghai. The family fortune is worth millions. Originally, I was reluctant to marry her off. Now, every performance in the hall requires more than 2,000 yuan, and four or five hundred are made, like a flower blooming. Although she gets a lump sum of money when she marries, if she doesn't marry, she can earn it in two performances. It doesn't matter if she helps me for a few more years. But I love this girl the most, Ruiyun. I really treat her like my own daughter. I just wish she was in my belly. Usually, I seem to hold her in my mouth, afraid that she will melt. Not to mention hitting her, I can't even bear to say a harsh word to her. Now, she's getting married at this age, and I'm really reluctant to say it." Her voice was a little sad, and tears seemed to be falling down. Zuo Shichen thought, "You don't need to cry crocodile tears. I know some things. It's probably that young master Zhang offered more money, so the auctioneer hammered it down." Is she really cherishing her adopted daughter and planning for her future? He couldn't bear it anymore and exposed her, saying, "I heard someone say that there are three customers who want your Anan." The elder aunt was surprised and said, "Huh? Did someone really say that outside? Yes, there are, but these two customers are not very good. It's okay to tell the Second Young Master, anyway, you've heard of them. One is surnamed Zhao, Zhao Qi, and the other is surnamed Wu, Wu San. They both said they wanted our Anan. But these two are not as good as young master Zhang. Second Young Master, although I am a person who eats hall food, marrying a person is a lifetime matter. First, I hope they don't come out again. Second, I hope they are happy after marriage. You think that Zhao Qi is young, but he has not been married to his wife for three years, and he is flirting outside. He is naturally a young master, but the economic power is still in the hands of his old father. The old man manages him fiercely, fearing that the young master will have money to come out and play. He only gives him a limited amount of money every month. He took Anan to go and cannot live in the old house, unless he wants to hide it from the family and rent a small mansion. This is a private niche."

More Than 100,000 Packages of Zhejiang Dry Cocoons Transported 122

A Large Batch of Cocoon Ships Will Arrive in Shanghai Within Days

The new dry cocoons of various Zhejiang provinces are piled up at the station and exposed to the sun and rain, waiting to be transported, and the Railway Bureau lacks vehicles. Although the silk factory industry association has repeatedly consulted with the traffic manager of the Railway Bureau, it was promised to stop loading passenger and cargo for two days to transport cocoon packages. However, the dry cocoons of various provinces are piled up like mountains, and the Shanghai factory needs cocoons very much. Therefore, the cocoon merchants hired hundreds of large barges and dozens of small wheels, and actively loaded and transported by water and land. In addition to the transportation by freight car, in the recent four or five days, a total of 350-60 cocoon ships from various provinces have arrived. The cocoon ships are full on both sides of the Suzhou River, with a total of more than 100,000 packages of new cocoons loaded. They are now hiring small workers to carry them to the store. A large batch of cocoon ships from Shaoxing will arrive in Shanghai within days.

Anhui and Jiangxi New Tea Summary 123

Most of the new teas in Wuyuan have not been sold. The market has been bleak in recent days. Except for the opening and trading of some southwestern villages, only 3/10 of the household tea on the north road is sold. No one has asked about the new tea of ​​Da Dayuan so far. The general tea households urgently need to apply the wages for making tea due to the famine and lack of rice, so they sell it at a low price. Recently, the new tea market has automatically fallen from 80 yuan to 50 yuan. Although the tea houses know that the price is cheap and can be handled, the food in this county is lacking and they are suffering from nowhere to transport the foreign stomach. It is difficult to force the previous opening and trading. Now there is no money to pay, so the mountain households who sold and did not sell are all crying. The ticket price in the market has gradually risen to more than 1,310 yuan due to the exhaustion of the current foreign currency. There is still a market and no cash. The tea money is urgently needed, and they have flocked to Jingzhen Wuwan to apply for foreign currency to save themselves.

The Qinghong Tea Shop in Fuliang has a good sales volume. The red tea in the northeast of Fuliang and the green tea in the south have recently fallen in mountain prices due to the narrow stomachs of foreign houses. The store village learned that the mountain prices were low, and took the opportunity to search for and manufacture baskets and transport them to Su, Hu, Zhenjing, Chang, Xi, and other ports. The stomach removal is quite bad. Nanchang Raozhou helps the store dealers to also gather in Fudi to buy, but Gaozhuang green tea is too low for the store village to sell, so they are transported to Wuyuan. The market price is from 60 yuan to 42 yuan.

Local News

Upstream Navigation Stagnant 126

Suspension of Transport to Changsha: Yesterday, a certain shipping company in this port received an urgent telegram from Hankou stating that a certain ship en route to Hunan had already returned to Yuezhou. Shipments bound for Changsha from Shanghai were to be temporarily suspended. The Hunan cargo on the various river steamers that had already left Shanghai was instructed to temporarily store the cargo in the Hankou warehouse when it arrived in Hankou for safety.

Hunan Ships All Suspended: The Taikoo Company's upstream vessel, the "Ji'an," set sail from Shanghai this morning, temporarily ordered to run the Yangtze River route, while also going to Shashi and Yichang, but not to Changsha. Two of the Nisshin Kisen Kaisha's Hunan route vessels have been suspended for the use of Japanese residents.

British and American Warships Rush Upstream: Foreign shipping on the Yangtze River is very extensive, and there are also a large number of foreigners in Hunan Province. In addition to the Japanese First Foreign Expeditionary Force, which has already dispatched six warships to the upper reaches for escort, the British Yangtze River flagship "Bee" has also carried Naval Vice Admiral Maclean to Changsha in haste. In addition, the American Yangtze River flagship "USS Isabel" also set sail from Shanghai yesterday, heading directly to Hunan to protect foreign residents.

Six Merchant Ships Diverted to Hankou: The first batch of six merchant ships from Guangdong to Shanghai, when passing Wusong on the 2nd of this month, were dispatched to Jiujiang along the river. Yesterday at noon, each ship also sent a telegram to Shanghai stating that when the ships arrived at Xunpu, they were immediately ordered to rush to Hankou without stopping. All ships immediately weighed anchor and headed west, and it is expected that they will arrive safely in Hankou today.

Silver Cheapness Affects Shipping 127

Large Quantities of Foreign Silver Arrive in Shanghai: The price of gold has soared, the price of silver has plummeted, and foreign silver continues to arrive in Shanghai. Since the National Government explicitly prohibited it, large bars from San Francisco, USA, continue to be imported. The previous "Asama Maru" loaded 1,373,321 taels of large bars, which were purchased by various banks in Shanghai. They wanted to unload them in Shanghai, but were prohibited by the Customs, so they changed to Hong Kong. A certain American ship also transported a batch of silver bars the other day, with a huge amount. To avoid the prohibition, they were not unloaded at the wharf. Today, the Japanese ship "Tatsuta Maru" arrived in Shanghai, and the ship also loaded a large quantity of silver bars purchased by Shanghai banking circles. They are currently planning to unload them, but it is not yet known whether they can land. On the 9th of this month, it was heard that another million taels of American silver would arrive in Shanghai, but the loading and unloading were very secretive, and no third party was allowed to know except the crew and bankers. According to the current situation, on average, the United States imports at least six batches of silver bars to Shanghai every month, with each batch being more than one million taels and at least 300,000 to 400,000 taels.

Japanese Sugar and Piece Goods Sharply Reduced: After the price of silver plummeted, the price of Japanese gold has also gradually soared. Chinese merchants in our country have stopped transporting most of the Japanese sugar and piece goods they ordered. It is found that the Nisshin Kisen Kaisha ships transport the most sugar to Shanghai, importing 10,000 to 20,000 bags each time. In the past ten days, the Japanese ships coming to Shanghai have reduced the import of sugar, rock sugar, and foreign cloth, which have always been the major commodities in trade with China. Last week, only a few thousand bags of Japanese sugar arrived, and foreign cloth was also scarce, a decrease of 60% to 70% compared to before.

European and American Imports Are Not Prosperous: Recently, the imported goods loaded on the various merchant ships coming to Shanghai from the United Kingdom have shown anomalies. The woolen goods and nankeen foreign goods from that country are as rare as morning stars. For example, a giant ship of over 10,000 tons arriving in Shanghai would normally have 300 tons of piece goods, but now it only has 20 to 30 tons. Steel products and military supplies are increasing daily. As for the New York cargo ships coming to Shanghai from the United States, except for the materials of various oil companies and the tobacco leaves ordered by foreign merchants, there are no other goods arriving in Shanghai. The maritime market has been severely affected by the cheapness of silver.

Inland Foreign Goods Suspended: The Yangtze River and coastal route ships in this port have recently not been transporting foreign goods to the various ports of the Yangtze River and the northern and southern oceans. Taikoo, Jardine, and Nisshin, etc., which used to transport the most foreign goods, have transported local goods from the mainland on their ships in the past ten days. From this alone, it can be known that foreign goods are being reduced everywhere in the mainland. According to Chinese ships, foreign goods exports have been equal to zero since the rise in gold prices. Nowadays, Chinese ships going to the Northern Ocean only carry 10% of exports, which can be described as extremely declining.

Gold Prices Eased Slightly Yesterday 128

Yesterday, the opening price of gold was 594 taels, with a maximum of 594.5 taels. The closing price in the afternoon was 580 taels. Silver shop gold was 82.5 yuan, slightly lower than yesterday. The world financial market can be affected by even the slightest thing. There is no so-called national boundary. Moreover, this port is close to the Japanese gold market and follows the Japanese side for transfers. Therefore, the status of Japanese gold coins today has a close relationship with us, which is also something that financial people cannot fail to know. According to the Japanese "Mainichi Shimbun," since the beginning of April, the Yokohama Specie Bank has purchased gold coins from the Bank of Japan for 50 million yen due to the shortage of overseas gold reserves. The reason for the shortage of its overseas gold reserves is due to the sluggishness of the Japanese silk market and the export bills being far less than the bank's expectations. As for the Bank of Japan, within the first month after the lifting of the gold embargo, a total of 70 million yen of gold coins flowed out, most of which were sold to the Specie Bank. At present, the Japanese foreign exchange situation is that there are very few export bills on the market, and the Bank of Japan has to continue to supply gold coins to the Specie Bank, so the future of its gold coins is not optimistic. In addition, after China banned the export of gold, the situation is even worse. The Sumitomo and Mitsui banks have been providing spiritual assistance for the lifting of the gold embargo, so they specialize in searching for cash in foreign groups. Now that their way of transporting cash from Shanghai to the United States has been prohibited by the Customs, the two banks have decided to increase overseas gold reserves for foreign exchange. In the future, if China does not lift the embargo, it will only have to purchase cash from the Bank of Japan, so Japanese gold reserves will gradually flow out, which will eventually affect the status of Japanese gold coins. It is found that the cash purchased by Japanese exchange banks in Shanghai has reached 35 million yen to date, but this is still not enough to offset the import bills for the first half of the year, and it is necessary to transport some more gold coins overseas. This means taking it from the Bank of Japan, and there is no other way. (Note: Japan's foreign trade has always been an excess of imports over exports, but it is an excess of exports over imports with China, so it often uses the money earned from selling goods to China to absorb gold coins in China to compensate other countries.)

Import and Export Industries Plummet 130

Most Cargo Ships Suspended

The soaring price of gold and the plummeting silver market have affected all industries, with the import industry being the most affected. Export commodities from various places are also very sluggish due to various reasons. Recently, the daily import and export of goods has decreased daily, reaching only one-third of the past. Small cargo boats and tugboats of various transportation companies are suspended in half due to lack of cargo to load. The Shanghai Transportation Company usually has 46 pairs of small boats and 5 tugboats, averaging about 50,000 tons of import and export cargo per day. Recently, it has only been about 20,000 tons, and there is a trend of further reduction in the future. The decline of the import and export industry is really an unprecedented phenomenon.

Red Cross Rescue of Wounded Soldiers 131

The departure of the Chinese Red Cross rescue team has been reported in previous newspapers. Yesterday (the 5th), at about 1:00 PM, 150 to 160 seriously wounded officers and soldiers were sent from the Nanjing Military Medical Department to the Mackenzie Road Station. A total of seven iron-roofed freight cars were attached. Upon arrival at the port, Wang Peiyuan, chairman of the Chinese Red Cross on Jiujiang Road, along with more than 40 people including secretaries, staff, nurses, and laborers, used the association's ambulances and hired four trucks from the Shanghai Loading Ground Company to transport them to the Tianjin Road Hospital in turn. It was not completed until 5:00 PM. When the soldiers' car arrived at the station, the Red Cross first gave each person a bowl of hot tea, and Chairman Wang personally examined each one. Those who were seriously injured were taken to the car in advance, with the most being those with broken feet, broken wrists, broken femurs, and broken humeri. One soldier had a bullet that penetrated from the left cheek to the right cheek, breaking the tongue and dragging it out of the mouth, which was extremely miserable. One person died on the way due to being unable to withstand the bumping. According to the wounded soldiers, the fighting near Lanfeng was the most fierce. Those who were lightly wounded were rescued, and many who were seriously wounded died on the spot. Some were rescued and then died. There were too few nurses on the way, and they urinated and defecated in the car. It was also difficult to eat. Now, with the Red Cross providing assistance, there is still hope for rebirth. Amidst the sad cries, there is also a sense of joy, which can be said to be a stroke of luck in misfortune.

Conference on Abolishing Likin 132

The General Assembly Postponed for One Month

The Ministry of Finance of the National Likin Abolition Conference specially appointed Councilor Li Jihong to come to Shanghai and use the Central Bank on the Bund as a preparation office to preside over the General Assembly. The opening ceremony of the General Assembly was originally scheduled to be held on the 1st of this month, but because the financial departments of the provinces and the special commissioners of the Ministry of Finance were unable to arrive in time, only the provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui had to announce a postponement. The meeting will be held after more than half of the representatives have arrived. In addition, the current financial authorities believe that the abolition of likin is important, and they are collecting opinions and formulating plans to implement them effectively and achieve practical results. Therefore, it was decided to postpone it for one month and change it to early August. Yesterday, the Ministry of Finance instructed Councilor Li to stay in Shanghai to receive the registered representatives and invite the representatives of the provinces that have arrived to hold a preparatory meeting to prepare in advance. Therefore, there are still two or three preparatory meetings before the General Assembly so that the General Assembly can shorten the time. It is heard that the scope of discussion at the preparatory meeting and the formulation of plans are roughly: special consumption tax belongs to the national tax, and business tax belongs to the local tax.

Aftermath of the Accidental Loss of the Arsenal 133

The propellant filling room near the Gaochangmiao West Fort of the Shanghai Arsenal suddenly exploded on the morning of the 2nd due to improper filling, killing 13 people and injuring 24. The details have been reported in the previous newspaper. The reporter of the Guowenshe went to inquire again yesterday. According to Section Chief Pang of the General Affairs Section of the factory, the number of seriously injured workers who died one after another due to their injuries until last night, including the previous ones, was 21. The compensation measures are now determined that the deceased will be given 100 yuan for funeral expenses and 500 yuan for each person. The foreman, Shi Changhua, will be given double compensation due to his many years in the factory, totaling 1,000 yuan. The injured will be given compensation after they recover and are discharged from the hospital. The memorial service can only be held after the coffins are first placed in a temporary location due to the fact that the families have no place to store the coffins and the preparation takes time. It has been agreed with the families. Therefore, the foreman, Shi Changhua, has already been buried today. Today, Factory Director Guo has reported the situation to the Ordnance Department and the General Headquarters.

Feng Wenyu, the newly appointed Director of the Salt Affairs Anti-Smuggling Bureau of the Five Districts of Jiangsu, was transferred from the Anti-Smuggling Bureau of Southern Anhui. After the oath, Supervising Official Zhen gave a speech, roughly saying that Minister of Finance Song established two general teams in advance for the purpose of rectifying salt affairs and anti-smuggling, and to understand the current situation of anti-smuggling in the country, sent supervisory committee members to various bureaus to conduct detailed investigations and report, and formulated an entire rectification plan to be implemented step by step. The five districts of Jiangsu are the important areas of land and water in the country. Director Feng has extensive experience in handling anti-smuggling affairs in Huainan, Fujian, and Southern Anhui, and is especially courageous in doing things. The Anti-Smuggling Department intends to use Director Feng's ability to start with the five districts of Jiangsu, promote it to the whole country, and in the future, the five districts of Jiangsu can be a model for the national anti-smuggling bureau. However, there should be a policy for handling affairs. Although anti-smuggling is now independent, all matters should be coordinated with the salt transportation envoy, transportation deputy, tax transportation bureau, audit branch, audit and supervision, and implemented in consultation and carried out jointly. If this can be done, the handling of affairs will not be isolated, and the tax revenue of anti-smuggling reform will be increased. It is hoped that Director Feng will use his strong perseverance and fighting spirit to enrich the country's tax revenue and increase the sales volume of merchants. I hope that what I expect and realize at today's swearing-in ceremony. Next, Zhou Xiangling, president of the Salt Merchants Association, gave a speech, roughly saying that it is a great honor to participate in Director Feng's swearing-in ceremony today. Salt merchants hope that the sales volume of the Anti-Smuggling Bureau will increase daily. The five districts of Jiangsu are located in an important area. Salt smuggling from Changlu and Shandong and various private salt fields in Zhejiang are pouring into the area. Last year, the remaining warlords left over from Jiangbei used the pretext of refugees fleeing to smuggle large amounts of private salt and hide weapons from Lianghuai. There were as many as 4,000 to 5,000 private salt boats coming south. The five districts of Jiangsu were unprepared in advance, resulting in a shortage of 20,000 to 30,000 introduction papers in the spring of this year, and the loss of national tax was 500,000 to 600,000. Huai private salt earns tens of times the profit by selling to Jiangsu, which has a huge impact and endless troubles. It is learned that Chief Wen of the Anti-Smuggling Department intends to mobilize 10 battalions of officers and soldiers from Huainan, Huaibei, and the five districts of Jiangsu to go to Yancheng, Funing, and Haizhou immediately to fundamentally block and stop the private ships from gathering. I am sorry that Director Feng will bear the heavy task of command. We believe that he will be able to stop the private salt from coming south. Today's swearing-in ceremony is held here. Next, Wang Shoushan gave a speech, roughly saying that President Zhou has explained the situation of private salt smuggling in the five districts of Jiangsu and the current important anti-smuggling affairs that should be handled. Salt affairs and anti-smuggling rely on a thorough plan, especially on sufficient strength. There are not many officers and soldiers in the five districts of Jiangsu, but the guns and ammunition are dilapidated and the salaries are insufficient, which is quite a restraint on the reform. At present, we should supplement the fine and sharp guns and ammunition, and at the same time, the officers and soldiers should appropriately increase the new salaries. With sufficient strength, we can stop the smuggling of private salt smugglers, and other rectification can be solved easily. Next, Liu Chunpu gave a speech. I have not seen the achievements of Director Feng in handling anti-smuggling in the past, but I will not exaggerate. However, he handled the prohibition of opium and protection of shipping in Jiangsu Province in Shanghai in the past year, and the achievements were remarkable. It is more difficult to prohibit opium than salt affairs. If opium can be stopped and blocked, salt affairs will definitely have more achievements. Next, Representative Tang Muyao of the Transportation Deputy and Representative He Zhenping of the County Party Department gave speeches one after another, mostly praising and encouraging. Finally, Director Feng replied, roughly saying that I was ordered by the Minister of Finance to be transferred from Southern Anhui to the Director of the Anti-Smuggling Bureau of the Five Districts of Jiangsu. Today, I will hold a supplementary swearing-in ceremony. I am deeply grateful to the Supervising Official, the representatives, and the guests for their presence and encouragement. The five districts of Jiangsu are an important area of land and water in the country. The smuggling of private salt from the north and south has a great impact on the national tax. I have not achieved any success in handling anti-smuggling in recent years. This time, I was ordered to come here. I will abide by the national laws and the teachings of the Supervising Official, the representatives, and the guests to work hard to rectify the anti-smuggling in order to increase the national tax. I hope that you, gentlemen, will guide and supervise me at any time so that I will not fail. I would like to thank you very much. The meeting was adjourned at 12:00.

Telegram Request 141

Reduce the Fare of the Chao-Shan Railway

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce of the Republic of China telegraphed the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Railways of the National Government in Nanjing yesterday, stating that the case of the Chao-Shan Railway fare being changed to silver dollars has been repeatedly telegraphed by the Bureau and the Federation to maintain the old system and continue to use silver cents. Later, the Civil Service Office of the National Government approved the Ministry of Railways' reply, stating that in order to comply with public opinion, the railway has been ordered to temporarily change the third-class ticket price from 7 silver dollars to 6.5 silver dollars, etc., and forwarded the letter to the Federation, which then notified the public. Now, it is reported that Chao-Shan citizens Xu Zongyan and others collectively telegraphed that the Chao-Shan Railway fare was originally high and more expensive than any railway in the country. For example, the state-owned Canton-Samshui Railway charges 2 silver cents for a third-class ticket for 30 miles. The Chao-Shan Railway should charge 5.5 silver cents for 80 miles. It now charges 7 silver cents, which is 1.5 silver cents more expensive. The Ministry of Railways said that the price it set has a deficit compared to the standard price set by the Ministry, which is really incomprehensible. 1. The Canton-Samshui Railway, the Canton-Kowloon Railway, and the Yuehan Railway currently charge silver cents. The Chao-Shan Railway is the only one that wants to change to silver dollars, which is extremely illegal. The Ministry of Railways said that the silver dollars are the method set by the Ministry and are uniform throughout the country. Since they are uniform throughout the country, why are the Canton-Samshui Railway, the Canton-Kowloon Railway, and the Yuehan Railway not uniform? Are these three railways not within the scope of the Ministry of Railways? This is obviously a state-owned railway, which is really incomprehensible. 2. Please telegraph and appeal to continue to collect silver cents before the national currency system is unified, and reduce the third-class ticket price to 5.5 silver cents according to the proportion of the Canton-Samshui Railway ticket fare. The second-class and first-class tickets and the fares of each station should be reduced proportionally, etc., in order to relieve the merchants and the people. We still implore you to telegraph a reply to show your compliance. President Lin Kanghou, Standing Committee Member Su Minsheng, Zhang Yuquan, Lu Guangji, Chen Riping, Li Kuian, Peng Chuzhi, etc. of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce of the Republic of China respectfully request your consideration.

Transportation Agencies Must Operate as Usual 142

On National Day

The Shanghai County Government received an order from the Construction Department of Jiangsu Province, stating that in order to facilitate transportation, long-distance bus companies should operate daily according to the prescribed hours and should not be interrupted. Recently, it has been found that long-distance bus companies in various provinces often suspend operations and rest on National Day, which is inconsistent with the purpose of facilitating transportation. It is ordered that the Department forward this order to all highway bureaus and long-distance bus companies under its jurisdiction for compliance. The County Government has forwarded the order to all companies under its jurisdiction for compliance yesterday.

Wusong Chamber of Commerce to be Wound Up 146

Future Change to Branch Office

The Chamber of Commerce Reorganization Committee sent a letter to the Wusong Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating that the Committee's 47th Standing Committee meeting determined that Article 5 of the Chamber of Commerce Law states, "However, prosperous districts and towns may also independently or jointly establish chambers of commerce," and Article 8 of the same law states, "Chambers of commerce shall establish offices within their regions, and may establish branch offices if deemed necessary due to special circumstances with the resolution of a members' meeting." The meeting discussed which article should be used as the basis for reorganizing the Wusong Chamber of Commerce, which is located within the city's jurisdiction, and requested instructions from the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs. It was noted that on May 12, a reply was received from the Shanghai Special Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, No. 3774, stating that a letter was received requesting instructions on whether the Wusong Chamber of Commerce should be allowed to continue to be established as a chamber of commerce or whether it should be reorganized as a branch office of the Special Municipal Chamber of Commerce. It was noted that the town had long been incorporated into the Special Municipality's jurisdiction, and its proximity to your Chamber of Commerce and convenient transportation suggested that it was not necessary to establish a separate chamber. It would be more appropriate to establish a branch office to promote commercial interests while maintaining a unified organization. In accordance with the reply, you are requested to comply with the instructions. Furthermore, at the Committee's 50th Standing Committee meeting on May 15, it was discussed and resolved to forward a letter to your Chamber of Commerce, requesting that it be wound up and handed over to the Committee immediately. It will be decided at the Chamber of Commerce's general meeting whether to establish a branch office to comply with the legal system. Accordingly, a letter is hereby sent for your information and compliance. To the Wusong Chamber of Commerce.

Municipal Government Orders Strict Enforcement of Opium Ban 147

The Municipal Government approved the request from the Anti-Opium Commission, stating that, in order to strictly enforce the opium ban and quickly seek to aid opium addicts, in accordance with Chapter 5, Article 15 of the Opium Ban Enforcement Regulations, all senior local governments should supervise their subordinate anti-opium agencies to strictly investigate and prohibit the smoking of opium or its substitutes within their jurisdictions. Once discovered, in addition to sending the offenders to court for punishment according to law, those with opium addiction should be ordered to quit within a specified period. This was submitted to the 38th Committee meeting for discussion, which was passed and sent for approval. The Municipal Government then immediately instructed the Public Security and Health Bureaus to comply.

Municipal Government Requests Abolition of Wusong Ship Tax 148

In this city, ship taxes are collected by an office established by the Finance Bureau, while Wusong also has a Wusong Sand Fishing Boat Tax Bureau. Shipowners generally feel burdened by the double taxation. Previously, shipowners such as Lu Yuankai and others submitted a request to the Ministry of Finance to review and exempt one of the taxes. The Ministry of Finance ordered the Municipal Finance Bureau to investigate and discuss the matter. Bureau Chief Xu Fu investigated and found that in December of the 17th year of the Republic (1928), the Executive Yuan issued the "National Financial Conference's Standards for Dividing National and Local Revenue," and ship tax was listed as the seventh item under local revenue. It is very clear that ship tax is a local tax. Since it is a local tax, it should naturally be collected by the local government. Wusong is under the jurisdiction of this city, so all ships that enter and dock at Wusong, whether they stay for a long time for trade or transit to the Yangtze River, are within the city's jurisdiction. Therefore, the collection of ship tax by the Municipal Government is naturally the obvious thing to do. If the ship tax collected by the Wusong Sand Fishing Boat Tax Bureau is indeed a national tax, then after the "Standards for Dividing National and Local Revenue" were passed and promulgated in the 17th year of the Republic (1928), ship tax belonged to local revenue, and there should no longer be any national tax collection. The ship tax collected by the Wusong Bureau has fundamentally ceased to exist and should have been abolished long ago. If the tax collected by the bureau is a Jiangsu local tax, it should especially not be collected by an agency established within the jurisdiction of this city, as it would be an intrusion. Not only would ships be subject to two taxes at the same time, causing hardship to merchants, but it would also confuse the administrative authority of the province and the city. Therefore, based on the previous submission, the Municipal Government requested the Ministry of Finance to order the abolition of the Wusong Sand Fishing Boat Tax Bureau.

Shanghai Residents Urgently Rescue

Two Million Disaster Victims in Shaanxi 150

Three Yuan Saves a Life

Heaven's misfortune has struck Shaanxi province. Since the 17th year of the Republic (1928), there has been continuous drought. Since last year, the disaster situation has worsened, with vast areas of barren land and no harvests. According to on-site investigation reports from various charitable organizations, the disaster areas are characterized by desolate fields, deserted villages with nine out of ten homes empty, and people dying and fleeing. Villages are deserted, beds are filled with unburied corpses, and roads are covered with starving people. Birds and dogs are devouring the corpses, a scene too terrible to witness. For three years, Shaanxi province has suffered from drought, and last winter, it suffered from snow disasters. The snow was over four or five feet deep, and even flying birds died along with the livestock. The starving people cried day and night in the icy and snowy conditions, shivering and starving under straw heaps and thatched huts. Suffering from both hunger and cold, countless people died from freezing and starvation every day. Since the beginning of spring, the situation has worsened as the food supply has been exhausted. At first, disaster victims sold their houses and slept in the wild to survive. Then, they sold their wives and children and cooked their children for food. Old and weak couples wandered along the roads, weeping and wailing in misery. This situation and scene makes us heartbroken. The survivors are all emaciated and scrawny, their voices hoarse and weak, and they collapse and die with a single stumble. They eat all the grass and tree bark, and even swallow stone flour (i.e., Guanyin clay), which leads to poisoning and death. Even cannibalism has occurred, just like the savages in Africa. Moreover, the disaster area is full of corpses, and the stench is overwhelming. As a result, epidemics are rampant in the spring, and the survivors are suffering from further disasters. This is a disaster rarely seen by mankind, but the people of Shaanxi are experiencing it all. According to investigations, the number of people who have died from starvation and disease has exceeded three million, and the number of displaced people is no less than five million. This is truly a great catastrophe in China, a rare disaster in history. There are now more than two million survivors crying out for help. If they are not provided with emergency relief, they will eventually starve to death. Last month, charitable organization representatives Zhu Qinglan, Li Zushen, and disaster victim representative Liu Zhizhou personally went to Shaanxi province to investigate and witnessed a situation even more tragic than reported in the newspapers. Their initial plan was to transport relief grain directly to Shaanxi province, but due to the long distance and inconvenient transportation, it would take more than a month to arrive. The relief would be too slow to help the desperate situation. Therefore, as a temporary measure, the only option is to purchase grain locally to barely sustain life. Then, wait for the relief grain to be transported in to continue the relief efforts. Currently, the price of grain in Shaanxi province is three yuan per dou (peck), and one person needs one dou of rice per month. Therefore, three yuan can save a life. We are still waiting for people from all walks of life to generously donate to support this life-saving cause. People in North China, including Tianjin and Beijing, were moved by the tragedy of the disaster and organized organizations such as the Shaanxi Disaster Relief Emergency Committee. Newspapers such as Ta Kung Pao and Yong Pao held emergency relief publicity weeks to collect donations. Such publicity inspired people and appealed to all circles, who responded with enthusiasm and contributed generously. Young students voluntarily saved their food expenses, and poor workers donated their hard-earned money. Some even pawned their clothes and sold their belongings to donate. Merchants, scholars, and women also generously donated large sums of money. Although the donors came from different classes and backgrounds, they all contributed their best, from as little as a dime to as much as tens of thousands of yuan. Their righteousness is admirable. Now, we are making further efforts to raise funds more widely and organize ten-person disaster relief groups. The method is simple and easy to implement. Every ten people form a group, and each member of each group forms another group. In this way, one becomes ten, ten becomes a hundred, a hundred becomes a thousand, and a thousand becomes ten thousand. Within a few days, a very large disaster relief group can be formed. Each person donates one yuan for relief and is responsible for introducing at least ten new members within 24 hours. In this way, a large sum of money can be collected in a short period of time. Currently, 6 million yuan is needed to save the two million disaster victims. Although the Tianjin and Beijing areas have been raising funds, the donors have already made their best efforts, but the amount is still a drop in the bucket in the disaster area. Moreover, three yuan per life is calculated based on one month's worth of food. After one month, even if the new wheat harvest is somewhat hopeful, only a small portion of the disaster victims will be able to support themselves. The vast majority of the disaster victims have no money. Therefore, we hope that all circles in Shanghai will understand the extremely serious situation in the disaster area. Those who have not responded to the emergency relief efforts in Tianjin and Beijing must not sit idly by. They must fulfill their humanitarian duty of mutual assistance, rise up quickly, save all entertainment and consumption expenses, and quickly work hard to donate. Donating three more yuan means saving one more life. No matter how difficult and challenging our current situation is, it is still better and more comfortable than the Shaanxi disaster victims in the hell on earth. Let each do their best and not worry that the disaster is too great or the effort is too small, but simply seek peace of mind. Donations can be directly remitted to General Zhu Ziqiao of the North China Disaster Relief Association in Tianjin. The two million Shaanxi compatriots who are on the verge of death are looking forward to it with longing. We hope that the people of South China will inspire their conscience, encourage each other, and work together to promote this righteous cause. If people are kind, who is not like us? We should be eager and brave to act quickly to provide assistance. Then, the two million survivors will have years of gratitude.

(C) After postal students were renamed postal workers, the original promotion examination method was virtually abolished. Should the authorities be requested to restore it? The meeting resolved to approve. (D) How should the pending issues of the union be actively handled? The meeting resolved to submit them to a joint meeting of the two unions for joint action. (E) The Standing Committee submitted a review of the salary rates of car drivers for discussion. The meeting resolved to approve it according to the review opinions and instructed the negotiation section to handle it. (F) Please nominate preparatory committee members for the first sports meeting of Shanghai postal workers. The meeting resolved to nominate Zhu Xuefan, Zhang Kechang, and Cheng Zuoqing as preparatory committee members for the sports meeting. The meeting adjourned.

Dock Workers Union: The 25th Standing Committee meeting was held yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM, chaired by Shen Wenyuan. Formalities as usual. The following items were discussed: (1) Change the date of the joint meeting of the fifth district's branches. The meeting resolved to convene it at the union at 2:00 PM this Sunday afternoon. (2) Date of convening the full executive committee meeting of the fourth district's labor union. The meeting resolved that in case of an accident, they should ask the secretariat for leave, otherwise their salary will be deducted. Those who are absent for three days will be dismissed. (5) The registration office in Yinxiang District is attached to the Bansha Factory Labor Union at No. 574, Xingrenli, Dongzhakou, and is requested to be filed. (7) Determine the date for the third district's office to convene a joint meeting of representatives from wharves that have not joined. The meeting resolved to hold it at this place at 1:00 PM this Sunday afternoon. (8) How should the outstanding monthly dues from various wharves received by the union each month be handled? The meeting resolved to send personnel to review it. If it is still not paid, the Municipal Civic Training Committee will be requested to review it. (9) Shen Wenyuan proposed that there are still a small number of dock workers in Zhoujiadu and Baijing in Pudong who have not joined the union. Should personnel be sent to persuade them to join? The meeting resolved to send personnel to persuade them to join first. (10) The meeting adjourned after discussion.

(1) Mr. Chen, the comprador of the company, informed us that starting from June 1st, all godown staff would receive a subsidy of two yuan for rice until the price of rice falls. Therefore, a letter was sent to Mr. Chen to discuss a satisfactory solution before a vote is taken. The Indian went to Godown 14A to cause trouble, resulting in a dispute with the godown manager Lu Dazhou. Mr. Chen, together with a Westerner, ordered the Indian to apologize to the godown and fined him four yuan, which was sent to the Chinese Red Cross Society to help with disaster relief, as a warning for the future. It was said that no such incident should happen again. (4) Chen Shinan of the third branch G godown reported that Gao Mou had spread rumors about goods on the ship going to Jinan, damaging the reputation of the godown. How should this be handled?
